Life of the Author

Biography of Ibn Abidin: Name and Lineage
Author's biography: name, lineage, birth, and early Quran memorization.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Ibn 'Abidin's full name, lineage, birth year, and explain the significance of his early Quran memorization for his scholarship.

Core Idea
Ibn 'Abidin's meticulous scholarship began with perfecting his Quran recitation after a chance correction.

Understanding the background of a great jurist deepens our appreciation of his works. This passage introduces the name, lineage, and early life of Muhammad Amin Ibn 'Abidin, the renowned Hanafi jurist whose writings form the bedrock of late Hanafi fatwa. His early dedication to Quranic perfection foreshadows the precision he would bring to fiqh and usul al-iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and lineage
Read the passage carefully and list the complete name: Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz... up to Zayn al-Abidin. Note the title 'Ibn 'Abidin' and the connection to Fatima al-Zahra.
The lineage is not just a genealogy; it establishes scholarly and spiritual authority.
2
Locate his birth year and place
Find the explicit mention of his birth: 1198 AH in Damascus, Syria. Also note his father's piety and the family's reputation.
Knowing the time and place contextualises his later works.
3
Describe his early Quran memorization and the correction incident
The passage states he memorised the Quran early. While reciting in his father's shop, a passerby corrected a slight error. This prompted him to seek out the best reciter, Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id al-Hamawi.
This anecdote illustrates his humility and desire for excellence.
4
Explain the significance of his lineage and early life
His noble lineage (to Zayn al-Abidin and Fatima) gives him both sharaf (honour) and a tradition of learning. His early pursuit of perfection in Quran recitation shows his commitment to precision, a hallmark of his fiqh works like Radd al-Muhtar.
This background helps a mufti assess the authority of his opinions.

هو العالم الجليل، والفاضل النبيل البحر العلامة، والحبر الفهامة، الجهبذ الفقيه، والذكى النبيه عمدة المتأخرين، وخاتمة المحققين، الحسيب النسيب، الأديب الأريب السيد محمد أمين بن السيد عمر، بن السيد عبدالعزيز بن السيد أحمد بن السيد عبد الرحيم بن السيد نجم الدين ابن السید محمد صلاح الدين الشهير بـ "عابدين"، وهكذا يتصل نسبه الشريف بالسيد الشريف الإمام زين العابدين إلى السيدة فاطمة البتول بنت سيد الوجود صلّى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم . هذا وقد ولد المترجم لأبوين كريمين عُرفا بالتقوى والصلاح، فوالده السيد عمر بن أحمد كان معروفًا بالتقوى، وكذلك والدته رحمها الله تعالى .
مولده ونشأته وحياته :
ولد رحمه الله تعالى في دمشق الشام لأسرة شرف ،وعلم وفضل ومجد، سنة ۱۱۹۸ للهجرة الشريفة .
ونشأ نشأة مباركة في حجر والده في حي القنوات، فحفظ القرآن الكريم في سن مبكرة. وكان يتردّد إلى دكان لوالده ؛ ليألف التجارة والكسب الحلال، وفي أثناءها كان يتلو القرآن الكريم، فاعترضه أحد المارة إذ سمعه ؛ لقراءته في محل عام ليس فيه استماع واعترض عليه للحن خفيف، فقام من ساعته، وسأل عن أقرأ أهل عصره، فدل على شيخ قراء زمانه العلامة، الشيخ محمد سعيد بن إبراهيم الحموي، المتوفى سنة ١٢٣٦هـ، فجود القرآن
Introduction to the Investigation. His Name and Lineage: V. Translation of the Author. Translation of the Author. He is the great scholar, the noble virtuous one, the sea of knowledge, the ocean of understanding, the clever jurist, the intelligent alert one, the foremost of the later scholars, the seal of the researchers, the noble and distinguished, the cultured and intelligent, Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn al-Sayyid Umar, ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-Aziz, ibn al-Sayyid Ahmad, ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-Rahim, ibn al-Sayyid Najm al-Din, ibn al-Sayyid Muhammad Salah al-Din, famously known as 'Abidin'. Thus his noble lineage connects to the noble Sayyid Imam Zayn al-Abidin to Sayyida Fatima al-Batul, daughter of the Master of Existence, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. The subject was born to noble parents known for piety and righteousness; his father al-Sayyid Umar ibn Ahmad was known for piety, as was his mother, may Allah have mercy on her. His Birth, Upbringing, and Life: He was born, may Allah have mercy on him, in Damascus, Syria, to a family of honor, knowledge, virtue, and glory, in the year 1198 AH. He grew up in a blessed upbringing in the care of his father in the al-Qanawat district. He memorized the Holy Quran at an early age. He used to go to his father's shop to accustom himself to trade and lawful earnings, and during that time he would recite the Holy Quran. A passerby objected upon hearing him because his recitation was in a public place not designated for listening, and he objected due to a slight mistake in recitation. So he immediately got up and asked about the best reciter of his time. He was directed to the leading teacher of recitation of his time, the scholar Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id ibn Ibrahim al-Hamawi, who died in 1236 AH. So he perfected the Quran recitation...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the author's biography, typically found in the introduction of a scholarly edition. It gives the full name and lineage of Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz... known as Ibn Abidin, tracing his lineage back to Imam Zayn al-Abidin and Fatima al-Zahra. It then describes his birth in 1198 AH in Damascus and his early life. He memorized the Quran at a young age and, while working in his father's shop, was corrected by a passerby for a slight error in recitation. This motivated him to seek out the best Quran teacher of his time, Sheikh Muhammad Sa'id al-Hamawi, and he perfected his recitation. The passage is largely biographical and sets the stage for understanding the author's scholarly background.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn 'Abidin): The author of the work, known as Ibn 'Abidin, a leading Hanafi jurist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which year was Ibn Abidin born?
A) 1198 AH
B) 1236 AH
C) 1210 AH
D) 1190 AH

Key Takeaway
Ibn 'Abidin's noble lineage and early dedication to Quranic accuracy underscore his scholarly authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Life of the Author

Ibn Abidin: Noble Lineage and Birth
Biographical opening with lineage and birth details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe Ibn Abidin's lineage and state his birth year and place.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's lineage traces back to the Prophet ﷺ through Imam Zayn al-Abidin, grounding his authority in noble descent.

This passage opens the biography of the great Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin, author of Radd al-Muhtar. Understanding his noble lineage and birth helps us appreciate the weight of his scholarly authority and the esteem in which he was held.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and lineage
Read the first lines of the Arabic to extract his complete name and the chain of ancestors, ending with Imam Zayn al-Abidin.
The author is Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz … famously known as Ibn Abidin.
2
Note the key lineage figure
Recognize that his lineage connects to Imam Zayn al-Abidin, the grandson of Imam Husayn, and ultimately to Fatima al-Zahra', daughter of the Prophet.
This establishes him as a sayyid (descendant of the Prophet).
3
Extract his birth year and place
Locate the sentence stating he was born in Damascus in 1198 AH.
This corresponds to 1784 CE.
4
Note the piety of his parents
Read the description of his father and mother as being known for taqwa and righteousness.
His father Sayyid Umar ibn Ahmad and his mother both had a reputation for piety.

هو العالم الجليل، والفاضل النبيل البحر العلامة، والحبر الفهامة، الجهبذ الفقيه، والذكى النبيه عمدة المتأخرين، وخاتمة المحققين، الحسيب النسيب، الأديب الأريب السيد محمد أمين بن السيد عمر، بن السيد عبدالعزيز بن السيد أحمد بن السيد عبد الرحيم بن السيد نجم الدين ابن السید محمد صلاح الدين الشهير بـ "عابدين"، وهكذا يتصل نسبه الشريف بالسيد الشريف الإمام زين العابدين إلى السيدة فاطمة البتول بنت سيد الوجود صلّى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم . هذا وقد ولد المترجم لأبوين كريمين عُرفا بالتقوى والصلاح، فوالده السيد عمر بن أحمد كان معروفًا بالتقوى، وكذلك والدته رحمها الله تعالى .
مولده ونشأته وحياته :
ولد رحمه الله تعالى في دمشق الشام لأسرة شرف ،وعلم وفضل ومجد، سنة ۱۱۹۸ للهجرة الشريفة .
ونشأ نشأة مباركة في حجر والده في حي القنوات، فحفظ القرآن الكريم في سن مبكرة. وكان يتردّد إلى دكان لوالده ؛ ليألف التجارة والكسب الحلال، وفي أثناءها كان يتلو القرآن الكريم، فاعترضه أحد المارة إذ سمعه ؛ لقراءته في محل عام ليس فيه استماع واعترض عليه للحن خفيف، فقام من ساعته، وسأل عن أقرأ أهل عصره، فدل على شيخ قراء زمانه العلامة، الشيخ محمد سعيد بن إبراهيم الحموي، المتوفى سنة ١٢٣٦هـ، فجود القرآن عليه، وحفظ الشاطبية والميدانية، والجزرية. وأخذ عنه الفقه الشافعي، فحفظ عنه الزبد ، وأخذ النحو والصرف وغيرهما من علوم الآلة، حتى أجازه بما تجوز له روايته إجازة عامة - وستأتى بإجازاته- ثم شاءت إرادة الله تعالى أن يتصل بعلامة زمانه الشيخ شاكر العقاد، الشهير بـ ابن مقدم سعد"، وتوسم فيه الخير، فأقرأه التفسير والحديث، والأصول، والفرائض، والتصوف والحساب، والمعقولات، وألزمه بالتحول إلى مذهب الإمام الأعظم، فقرأ عليه كثيراً من كتب الفقه كـ" ملتقى الأبحر "
و "كنز الدقائق " وشرحه " البحر الرائق" و "الدراية" و "الهداية" وغير ذلك . ثم بدأ بقراءة "الدر المختار " مع جماعة من الأعلام، أشهرهم الشيخ سعيد الحلبي، وقد كان لاتصال العلامة ابن عابدين بشيخه الشيخ شاکر، أثر كبير في سلوكه العلمي والروحي، حيث لزمه ملازمة تامة طيلة سبع سنوات كاملة، كان خلالها يصله بشيوخه، ويستجيز هم له حتى علا سنده وارتفع قدره، وأخذ عنه الطريقة القادرية التى كان دائم المحافظة عليها، ثم ما لبث العلامة العقاد أن انتقل إلى رحمة الله تعالى، فاختير العلامة الناسك، الفقيه المربى ، الشيخ سعيد الحلبي خليفة عن الشيخ العقاد ؛ لإتمام ما بدأ به ؛ لأنه كان أنبه من في الحلقة، وشيخ الحنفية في عصره، وقد كان يحب ابن عابدين حبا جما ، لا يفتتح الدرس حتى يحضر ، بينما كان الآخر معه في غاية الأدب والإجلال، وكان درس "الدر" يقرأ بجوار المسجد الأموى قبل الفجر.
سمته وهيئته :
كان المترجم ذا هيئة حسنة، وخلقه مستحسنة جميلة، جعلته مألوفًا محبوبا عند كل من يراه .
يقول ابنه السعيد، السيد محمد علاء
Biography of the Author: He is the great scholar, the noble virtuous one, the ocean of knowledge, the ocean of the learned, the one of profound understanding, the jurist of acute intellect, the intelligent and perspicacious, the leader of the later scholars, the seal of the verifiers, the noble and high-born, the cultured and sagacious, Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn al-Sayyid Umar, ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-‘Aziz ibn al-Sayyid Ahmad ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-Rahim ibn al-Sayyid Najm al-Din ibn al-Sayyid Muhammad Salah al-Din, famous as ‘Abidin. Thus his noble lineage connects to the noble master Imam Zayn al-‘Abidin down to Lady Fatima al-Batul, daughter of the Master of Existence, may Allah bless him and grant him peace and his family. He was born to noble parents known for piety and righteousness: his father Sayyid Umar ibn Ahmad was known for piety, and likewise his mother, may Allah have mercy on her. His birth, upbringing, and life: He was born in Damascus of Syria, to a family of honor, knowledge, virtue, and glory, in the year 1198 AH. He was raised in a blessed upbringing in his father's care in the Qanawat district, memorizing the Noble Qur'an at an early age. He used to frequent his father's shop to become accustomed to trade and lawful earning, and while there he would recite the Qur'an. A passerby confronted him when he heard him reciting in a public place not meant for listening and objected to a slight error. So he stood up immediately and asked about the most skilled reciter of his time. He was directed to the leading reciter of his era, the scholar Shaykh Muhammad Sa‘id ibn Ibrahim al-Hamawi, who died in 1236 AH. He recited the Qur'an correctly to him, and memorized the Shatibiyya, Maydaniyya, and Jazariyya. He studied Shafi‘i fiqh with him, memorizing al-Zubad. He also studied grammar, morphology, and other instrumental sciences until he was given a general license to transmit what he had learned – his licenses will be mentioned later. Then Allah willed that he connect with the great scholar of his time, Shaykh Shakir al-‘Aqqad, famous as Ibn Muqaddam Sa‘d, who perceived goodness in him. He taught him Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara’id, Tasawwuf, Arithmetic, and Rational Sciences, and obliged him to convert to the school of the Great Imam [Abu Hanifa]. He studied with him many books of fiqh such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa’iq, its commentary al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, al-Diraya, al-Hidaya, and others. Then he began to study al-Durr al-Mukhtar with a group of eminent scholars, most notably Shaykh Sa‘id al-Halabi. The connection of ‘Allama Ibn ‘Abidin with his teacher Shaykh Shakir had a great impact on his academic and spiritual conduct, as he remained in close companionship with him for a full seven years during which he connected him with his teachers and obtained licenses for him, until his chain became elevated and his status rose. He also received from him the Qadiri order, which he constantly maintained. Then, before long, ‘Allama al-‘Aqqad passed away, and the devout scholar, jurist, and educator Shaykh Sa‘id al-Halabi was chosen as his successor to complete what he had begun, for he was the most prominent in the circle and the Hanafi shaykh of his era. He greatly loved Ibn ‘Abidin; he would not start a lesson until he arrived, while the latter showed utmost respect and veneration. The lesson on al-Durr would be read near the Umayyad Mosque before Fajr. His appearance and demeanor: The author had a pleasing appearance and admirable, beautiful character, making him familiar and beloved to all who saw him. His son al-Sa‘id Sayyid Muhammad ‘Ala’ says:
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author, the renowned Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin (Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahim ibn Najm al-Din ibn Muhammad Salah al-Din, famously known as Ibn Abidin). It begins by praising his scholarly stature, then traces his noble lineage back to Imam Zayn al-Abidin and ultimately to Fatima al-Zahra', the daughter of the Prophet (peace be upon him). He was born in Damascus in 1198 AH (1784 CE) into a pious family. His early education included Qur'an memorization and recitation (tajweed) with notable teachers. He initially studied Shafi'i fiqh with Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id al-Hamawi. Later, his pivotal teacher Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad guided him to convert to the Hanafi madhhab and instructed him in various Islamic sciences, including Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara'id, and logic. Ibn Abidin studied key Hanafi texts such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Hidaya. He also studied al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. The biography emphasizes his close companionship with his teachers and his spiritual link to the Qadiri order. The passage concludes with a description of his noble character and the testimony of his son, indicating that this biography is the basis for understanding the author's authority in later Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn ‘Abidin): The common name for the author, Muhammad Amin al-Hanafi, the jurist.
مذهب الإمام الأعظم (Madhhab al-Imam al-A‘zam): The Hanafi school of jurisprudence.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Haskafi, which Ibn Abidin commented on in Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what year was Ibn Abidin born?
A) 1198 AH
B) 1236 AH
C) 1212 AH
D) 1180 AH

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abidin was born in 1198 AH into a noble family tracing back to the Prophet, establishing his prestige.

Ibn Abidin: Education and Conversion to the Hanafi School
Detailed account of Ibn Abidin's educational journey and madhhab conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount Ibn Abidin's key teachers and explain his conversion from Shafi'i to Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's conversion from Shafi'i to Hanafi school under Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad shaped him into the preeminent late Hanafi authority.

This part of Ibn Abidin's biography details his early studies and the pivotal moment when he switched madhhabs under the guidance of his teacher. This conversion was not a rejection but an embrace of the Hanafi school's strength in his context. Understanding this journey helps us appreciate the depth of his later work.

Guided Path
1
Identify his early teacher for tajweed and Shafi'i fiqh
Locate the name of the teacher with whom he studied Qur'an recitation and Shafi'i fiqh.
Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id al-Hamawi (d. 1236 AH).
2
Note his study with Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad
Find the passage where he meets Shaykh Shakir, who taught him many sciences and obliged him to convert to Hanafi madhhab.
Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad, known as Ibn Muqaddam Sa'd.
3
Understand why he converted to Hanafi school
The text does not give a reason, but the teacher 'obliged' him; this reflects the common practice of scholars choosing a madhhab for study.
Conversion was likely for academic focus, not rejection of Shafi'i.
4
List the major Hanafi texts he studied
Extract the titles mentioned: Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Diraya, al-Hidaya, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
These are core Hanafi texts.
5
Recognize the role of Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi
Note that after Shaykh Shakir died, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi continued teaching al-Durr al-Mukhtar and was the head of the study circle.
He was the prominent Hanafi shaykh of the time.

هو العالم الجليل، والفاضل النبيل البحر العلامة، والحبر الفهامة، الجهبذ الفقيه، والذكى النبيه عمدة المتأخرين، وخاتمة المحققين، الحسيب النسيب، الأديب الأريب السيد محمد أمين بن السيد عمر، بن السيد عبدالعزيز بن السيد أحمد بن السيد عبد الرحيم بن السيد نجم الدين ابن السید محمد صلاح الدين الشهير بـ "عابدين"، وهكذا يتصل نسبه الشريف بالسيد الشريف الإمام زين العابدين إلى السيدة فاطمة البتول بنت سيد الوجود صلّى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم . هذا وقد ولد المترجم لأبوين كريمين عُرفا بالتقوى والصلاح، فوالده السيد عمر بن أحمد كان معروفًا بالتقوى، وكذلك والدته رحمها الله تعالى .

ولد رحمه الله تعالى في دمشق الشام لأسرة شرف ،وعلم وفضل ومجد، سنة ۱۱۹۸ للهجرة الشريفة .
ونشأ نشأة مباركة في حجر والده في حي القنوات، فحفظ القرآن الكريم في سن مبكرة. وكان يتردّد إلى دكان لوالده ؛ ليألف التجارة والكسب الحلال، وفي أثناءها كان يتلو القرآن الكريم، فاعترضه أحد المارة إذ سمعه ؛ لقراءته في محل عام ليس فيه استماع واعترض عليه للحن خفيف، فقام من ساعته، وسأل عن أقرأ أهل عصره، فدل على شيخ قراء زمانه العلامة، الشيخ محمد سعيد بن إبراهيم الحموي، المتوفى سنة ١٢٣٦هـ، فجود القرآن عليه، وحفظ الشاطبية والميدانية، والجزرية. وأخذ عنه الفقه الشافعي، فحفظ عنه الزبد ، وأخذ النحو والصرف وغيرهما من علوم الآلة، حتى أجازه بما تجوز له روايته إجازة عامة - وستأتى بإجازاته- ثم شاءت إرادة الله تعالى أن يتصل بعلامة زمانه الشيخ شاكر العقاد، الشهير بـ ابن مقدم سعد"، وتوسم فيه الخير، فأقرأه التفسير والحديث، والأصول، والفرائض، والتصوف والحساب، والمعقولات، وألزمه بالتحول إلى مذهب الإمام الأعظم، فقرأ عليه كثيراً من كتب الفقه كـ" ملتقى الأبحر "
و "كنز الدقائق " وشرحه " البحر الرائق" و "الدراية" و "الهداية" وغير ذلك . ثم بدأ بقراءة "الدر المختار " مع جماعة من الأعلام، أشهرهم الشيخ سعيد الحلبي، وقد كان لاتصال العلامة ابن عابدين بشيخه الشيخ شاکر، أثر كبير في سلوكه العلمي والروحي، حيث لزمه ملازمة تامة طيلة سبع سنوات كاملة، كان خلالها يصله بشيوخه، ويستجيز هم له حتى علا سنده وارتفع قدره، وأخذ عنه الطريقة القادرية التى كان دائم المحافظة عليها، ثم ما لبث العلامة العقاد أن انتقل إلى رحمة الله تعالى، فاختير العلامة الناسك، الفقيه المربى ، الشيخ سعيد الحلبي خليفة عن الشيخ العقاد ؛ لإتمام ما بدأ به ؛ لأنه كان أنبه من في الحلقة، وشيخ الحنفية في عصره، وقد كان يحب ابن عابدين حبا جما ، لا يفتتح الدرس حتى يحضر ، بينما كان الآخر معه في غاية الأدب والإجلال، وكان درس "الدر" يقرأ بجوار المسجد الأموى قبل الفجر.
سمته وهيئته :
كان المترجم ذا هيئة حسنة، وخلقه مستحسنة جميلة، جعلته مألوفًا محبوبا عند كل من يراه .
يقول ابنه السعيد، السيد محمد علاء
Biography of the Author: He is the great scholar, the noble virtuous one, the ocean of knowledge, the ocean of the learned, the one of profound understanding, the jurist of acute intellect, the intelligent and perspicacious, the leader of the later scholars, the seal of the verifiers, the noble and high-born, the cultured and sagacious, Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn al-Sayyid Umar, ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-‘Aziz ibn al-Sayyid Ahmad ibn al-Sayyid Abd al-Rahim ibn al-Sayyid Najm al-Din ibn al-Sayyid Muhammad Salah al-Din, famous as ‘Abidin. Thus his noble lineage connects to the noble master Imam Zayn al-‘Abidin down to Lady Fatima al-Batul, daughter of the Master of Existence, may Allah bless him and grant him peace and his family. He was born to noble parents known for piety and righteousness: his father Sayyid Umar ibn Ahmad was known for piety, and likewise his mother, may Allah have mercy on her. His birth, upbringing, and life: He was born in Damascus of Syria, to a family of honor, knowledge, virtue, and glory, in the year 1198 AH. He was raised in a blessed upbringing in his father's care in the Qanawat district, memorizing the Noble Qur'an at an early age. He used to frequent his father's shop to become accustomed to trade and lawful earning, and while there he would recite the Qur'an. A passerby confronted him when he heard him reciting in a public place not meant for listening and objected to a slight error. So he stood up immediately and asked about the most skilled reciter of his time. He was directed to the leading reciter of his era, the scholar Shaykh Muhammad Sa‘id ibn Ibrahim al-Hamawi, who died in 1236 AH. He recited the Qur'an correctly to him, and memorized the Shatibiyya, Maydaniyya, and Jazariyya. He studied Shafi‘i fiqh with him, memorizing al-Zubad. He also studied grammar, morphology, and other instrumental sciences until he was given a general license to transmit what he had learned – his licenses will be mentioned later. Then Allah willed that he connect with the great scholar of his time, Shaykh Shakir al-‘Aqqad, famous as Ibn Muqaddam Sa‘d, who perceived goodness in him. He taught him Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara’id, Tasawwuf, Arithmetic, and Rational Sciences, and obliged him to convert to the school of the Great Imam [Abu Hanifa]. He studied with him many books of fiqh such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa’iq, its commentary al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, al-Diraya, al-Hidaya, and others. Then he began to study al-Durr al-Mukhtar with a group of eminent scholars, most notably Shaykh Sa‘id al-Halabi. The connection of ‘Allama Ibn ‘Abidin with his teacher Shaykh Shakir had a great impact on his academic and spiritual conduct, as he remained in close companionship with him for a full seven years during which he connected him with his teachers and obtained licenses for him, until his chain became elevated and his status rose. He also received from him the Qadiri order, which he constantly maintained. Then, before long, ‘Allama al-‘Aqqad passed away, and the devout scholar, jurist, and educator Shaykh Sa‘id al-Halabi was chosen as his successor to complete what he had begun, for he was the most prominent in the circle and the Hanafi shaykh of his era. He greatly loved Ibn ‘Abidin; he would not start a lesson until he arrived, while the latter showed utmost respect and veneration. The lesson on al-Durr would be read near the Umayyad Mosque before Fajr. His appearance and demeanor: The author had a pleasing appearance and admirable, beautiful character, making him familiar and beloved to all who saw him. His son al-Sa‘id Sayyid Muhammad ‘Ala’ says:
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author, the renowned Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin (Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahim ibn Najm al-Din ibn Muhammad Salah al-Din, famously known as Ibn Abidin). It begins by praising his scholarly stature, then traces his noble lineage back to Imam Zayn al-Abidin and ultimately to Fatima al-Zahra', the daughter of the Prophet (peace be upon him). He was born in Damascus in 1198 AH (1784 CE) into a pious family. His early education included Qur'an memorization and recitation (tajweed) with notable teachers. He initially studied Shafi'i fiqh with Shaykh Muhammad Sa'id al-Hamawi. Later, his pivotal teacher Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad guided him to convert to the Hanafi madhhab and instructed him in various Islamic sciences, including Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara'id, and logic. Ibn Abidin studied key Hanafi texts such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and al-Hidaya. He also studied al-Durr al-Mukhtar with Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. The biography emphasizes his close companionship with his teachers and his spiritual link to the Qadiri order. The passage concludes with a description of his noble character and the testimony of his son, indicating that this biography is the basis for understanding the author's authority in later Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn ‘Abidin): The common name for the author, Muhammad Amin al-Hanafi, the jurist.
مذهب الإمام الأعظم (Madhhab al-Imam al-A‘zam): The Hanafi school of jurisprudence.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Haskafi, which Ibn Abidin commented on in Radd al-Muhtar.

Life of the Author

The Author's Scholarly Journey: Conversion and Isnad
Narrative of the author's early education and conversion to Hanafi madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the stages of the author's scholarly formation and explain why isnad and madhhab conversion are critical in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti's authority is built on a solid chain of transmission and deep study under recognized masters.

The biography of the author (likely Ibn 'Abidin) illustrates the classical path of Hanafi scholarship. He began with Shafi'i fiqh and instrumental sciences, then was directed by his teacher Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad to convert to the Hanafi madhhab. Under al-Aqqad, he studied core Hanafi texts and remained in his company for seven years, gaining a strong isnad and spiritual training in the Qadiriyya path. This lesson examines how these elements—isnad, madhhab adherence, and systematic study—form the foundation of a mufti's authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's early studies
Look at what he studied before meeting al-Aqqad: he memorized Shatibiyyah, Maydanigah, Jazariyyah, and studied Shafi'i fiqh, grammar, morphology, and other instrumental sciences. This shows a broad foundational training.
Shatibiyyah is a poem on qira'at; Maydanigah is a Hanafi text, but here it's listed as part of his early studies.
2
Note the role of Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad
Al-Aqqad compelled him to convert to the Hanafi madhhab of Abu Hanifa. This conversion is significant for a mufti—it ties the fatwa to the school's principles and chain.
Conversion to Hanafi madhhab was a formal step, reflecting the importance of madhhab affiliation in fatwa.
3
List the major Hanafi texts studied
Under al-Aqqad, he read Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and later al-Durr al-Mukhtar. These are authoritative Hanafi works from different levels of commentary.
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is the matn (text) that later became the basis for Ibn 'Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar.
4
Assess the impact of seven-year companionship
He stayed with al-Aqqad for seven full years, during which al-Aqqad connected him with his own teachers and sought ijazat for him. This elevated his chain (isnad) and rank. Also, he received the Qadiriyya spiritual path.
The isnad (chain of transmission) is crucial for the reliability of hadith, but also for the authority of fiqh and fatwa in the classical tradition.

يقول ابنه السعيد، السيد محمد علاء الدين آفندی رحمه الله : " وكان رحمه الله تعالى طويل القامة، شين الأعضاء والأنامل أبيض اللون أسود الشعر فيه قليل الشيب، لو عد شيبه لعد ، مقرون الحاجبين ذا هيبة ووقار، وهيئة مستحسنة ونضار جميل الصورة حسن السريرة، يتلألأ وجهه نوراً ، حسن البشر والصحبة، من اجتمع به لا يكاد بنساه لطلاوة كلامه ولين جانبه و تمام تواضعه على الوجه المشروع كثير الفوائد لمن صاحبه والمفاكهة، ومجلسه مشتمل على الآداب وحسن المنطق والإكرام للواردين عليه من أهله ومحبيه وتلامذته ومصاحبيه. كل من جالسه يقول في نفسه : أنا أعز عنده من ولده مجلسه محفوظ من الفحش والغيبة، والتكلم بما لا يعنى . لا تخلو أوقاته من الكتابة والإفادة، والمراجعة للمسائل. صادق اللهجة ذا فراسة إيمانية وحكمة لقمانية . متين الدين لا تأخذه في الله لومة لائم.. صداعا بالحق ولو عند الحاكم الجائر. تهابه الحكام والقضاة وأهل السياسة. كانت دمشق في زمنه أعدل البلاد وللشرع بها ناموس عظيم لايتجاسر أحد على ظلم أحد ولا على إثبات حق بغير وجه شرعي، ولا في غالب البلاد القريبة منها ؛ فإنه كان إذا حكم على أحد بغير وجه شرعی خاءه المحكوم عليه بصورة حجة القاضي فيفتيه ببطلانه ويراجع القاضى فينفذ فتواه وفل أن تقع واقعه مهمة، أو مشكلة مذلهمة في سائر البلاد أو بقية المدن الإسلامية أو قراها إلا ويستفتى فيها مع كثرة العلماء الأكابر والمفتين فى كل مدينة. وكانت أعراب البوادي إذا وصلت إليهم فتواه لا يختلفون فيها مع جهلهم بالشريعة المطهرة. وكانت كلمته نافذة، وشفاعته مقبولة، وكتابته ميمونة . ما كتب لأحد شيئًا إلا وانتفع به ؛ لصدق نيته وحسن سريرته، وقوة يقينه وشدة دينه وصلابته فيه. تكملة رد المحتار) (

Introduction to the verification
Biography of the author
...and he memorized the Shatibiyyah and Maydanigah and Jazariyyah. And he took from him Shafi'i fiqh, and memorized from him al-Zubad, and studied grammar and morphology and other instrumental sciences, until he granted him a general permission for whatever he was allowed to narrate - and his permissions will come later - then the will of Allah Almighty decreed that he connect with the scholar of his time, Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad, famous as Ibn Muqaddam Sa'd, and he perceived good in him, so he taught him Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara'id, Tasawwuf, Arithmetic, and Rational sciences, and compelled him to convert to the madhhab of the Greatest Imam. So he read many books of fiqh with him, such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and others. Then he began reading al-Durr al-Mukhtar with a group of eminent scholars, the most famous of whom was Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. And the connection of 'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin with his shaykh Shakir had a great impact on his academic and spiritual conduct, as he adhered to him completely for seven full years, during which he connected him with his own teachers and sought permissions for him, until his chain became elevated and his rank rose. He took from him the Qadiriyya path, which he constantly maintained. Then soon after, 'Allamah al-Aqqad passed away to the mercy of Allah, so the devout scholar, the jurist and educator, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi, was chosen as the successor to Shaykh al-Aqqad to complete what he had started, because he was the most prominent in the study circle and the Shaykh of the Hanafis in his time. He had immense love for Ibn 'Abidin; he would not begin the lesson until he arrived, while the other was with him in utmost politeness and reverence. The lesson of al-Durr was read near the Umayyad Mosque before dawn.
His character and appearance:
The subject of this biography had a good appearance and beautiful praiseworthy character, which made him familiar and beloved to everyone who saw him.
His blessed son, Sayyid Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din Afandi (may Allah have mercy on him) says: "He (may Allah have mercy on him) was tall, well-proportioned in limbs and fingers, white-skinned, black-haired with a little grey; if his grey hairs were counted, they would be few. He had joined eyebrows, with dignity and majesty, a pleasing appearance and freshness, beautiful face, good inner self, his face radiated light, good cheer and companionship. Whoever met him would hardly forget him, due to the sweetness of his speech, his gentleness, and his complete humility in the prescribed manner. He was of great benefit to those who accompanied him, and he enjoyed pleasant conversation. His gathering included etiquette, good speech, and honor for those who came to him from his family, his lovers, his students, and his companions. Everyone who sat with him said to themselves: 'I am dearer to him than his own child.' His gathering was free from obscenity, backbiting, and speaking about what does not concern him. His times were never free from writing, teaching, and reviewing issues. He was truthful in speech, possessed of intuitive faith and Luqman-like wisdom. He was firm in religion, and no blame of a blamer could affect him in matters of Allah. He spoke the truth even before an unjust ruler. The rulers, judges, and politicians were in awe of him. Damascus in his time was the most just of cities, and the Shari'ah had great prestige there; no one dared to oppress anyone or establish a right without a legal basis, nor in most of the nearby cities. For if a judge ruled against someone without legal justification, the one ruled against would bring the judge's document to him, and he would give a fatwa of its nullity and refer the matter back to the judge, who would execute his fatwa. And there was no important or perplexing incident in all the Islamic lands or the rest of Islamic cities or villages but he would be asked for a fatwa regarding it, despite the abundance of senior scholars and muftis in every city. And the bedouin Arabs, when his fatwa reached them, they would not differ regarding it despite their ignorance of the pure Shari'ah. His word was effective, his intercession accepted, and his writings blessed. He never wrote anything for anyone except that he benefited from it, due to the sincerity of his intention, his good inner self, the strength of his certainty, the intensity of his religion, and his firmness in it. (Takmilah Radd al-Muhtar) (6
His habits and ethics:
In this regard, the author's son, the scholar Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din Afandi, member of the scientific society, compiler of the legal journal on the just rulings during the time of the Ottoman Caliphate, says:

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author (likely Ibn 'Abidin or the author of the original text). It begins by detailing his early studies: he memorized important texts (Shatibiyyah, Maydanigah, Jazariyyah) and studied Shafi'i fiqh before being directed by Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad to convert to the Hanafi madhhab. Under Shaykh al-Aqqad, he studied major Hanafi works such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and later al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His association with Shaykh al-Aqqad lasted seven years, during which he received spiritual training (particularly the Qadiriyya path) and a strong chain of transmission. After al-Aqqad's death, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi took over as his mentor. The description emphasizes the author's excellent character, physical appearance, and piety. His influence was such that his fatwas were accepted across the Islamic world, even by bedouins, and his word was effective with rulers. The passage concludes with a note about the author's habits and ethics, quoting his son. This biography sets the context for the author's authority in Hanafi fiqh and fatwa, reflecting the high standards of learning and conduct expected of a mufti.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-'Allamah): An honorific title for a highly learned scholar, used repeatedly for the author and his teachers.
المذهب الإمام الأعظم (al-madhhab al-imam al-a'zam): The Hanafi madhhab, attributed to Abu Hanifa, who is called the Greatest Imam.
الطريقة القادرية (al-tariqah al-qadiriyyah): A Sufi order attributed to 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, which the author practiced and maintained.
الإسناد (al-isnad): The chain of transmission of knowledge, linking the student to earlier authorities; crucial for the reliability of fatwa and teaching.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): A permission granted by a scholar to a student to teach or transmit certain texts or subjects.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's authority is grounded in a recognized chain of transmission and systematic study of the madhhab's core texts under qualified teachers.

The Mufti's Character and Moral Authority
Description of the author's appearance, character, and the impact of his fatwas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the moral qualities that made the author an authoritative mufti and explain how these qualities contributed to the acceptance of his fatwas.

Core Idea
A mufti's moral integrity and adherence to the Shari'ah give his fatwas authority even over rulers and the uneducated.

The biography continues with a vivid description of the author's physical appearance and character. His tall stature, dignified bearing, and radiant face are noted. More importantly, his moral virtues—truthfulness, humility, fearlessness in speaking the truth, and firmness in religion—are emphasized. These qualities made his fatwas accepted across the Islamic world, from judges to bedouins. This lesson explores the ethical dimensions of a mufti's life as essential for his role.

Guided Path
1
List physical traits
The text describes him as tall, fair-skinned, black-haired with a little grey, joined eyebrows, dignified. These are mentioned to show his pleasing appearance which made him beloved.
Physical description is part of the classical biographical tradition.
2
Identify moral virtues
Key virtues: humility, truthfulness, firmness in religion, no fear of blame, speaking truth before unjust rulers, generosity, free from obscenity and backbiting. His gathering was full of adab and benefit.
These match the classical adab al-mufti requirements.
3
Understand the effect on fatwa acceptance
Because of his character, his fatwas were accepted by judges, rulers, and even bedouins. They were considered final and not disputed. This shows that a mufti's moral authority directly impacts the efficacy of his fatwas.
The passage says: 'And the bedouin Arabs, when his fatwa reached them, they would not differ regarding it.'
4
Connect to mufti adab
In Hanafi usul al-iftaa, a mufti must be pious, truthful, and just. This biography exemplifies those conditions.
Refer to the mufti's conditions in classical texts like Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti.

Introduction to the verification
Biography of the author
...and he memorized the Shatibiyyah and Maydanigah and Jazariyyah. And he took from him Shafi'i fiqh, and memorized from him al-Zubad, and studied grammar and morphology and other instrumental sciences, until he granted him a general permission for whatever he was allowed to narrate - and his permissions will come later - then the will of Allah Almighty decreed that he connect with the scholar of his time, Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad, famous as Ibn Muqaddam Sa'd, and he perceived good in him, so he taught him Tafsir, Hadith, Usul, Fara'id, Tasawwuf, Arithmetic, and Rational sciences, and compelled him to convert to the madhhab of the Greatest Imam. So he read many books of fiqh with him, such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and others. Then he began reading al-Durr al-Mukhtar with a group of eminent scholars, the most famous of whom was Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. And the connection of 'Allamah Ibn 'Abidin with his shaykh Shakir had a great impact on his academic and spiritual conduct, as he adhered to him completely for seven full years, during which he connected him with his own teachers and sought permissions for him, until his chain became elevated and his rank rose. He took from him the Qadiriyya path, which he constantly maintained. Then soon after, 'Allamah al-Aqqad passed away to the mercy of Allah, so the devout scholar, the jurist and educator, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi, was chosen as the successor to Shaykh al-Aqqad to complete what he had started, because he was the most prominent in the study circle and the Shaykh of the Hanafis in his time. He had immense love for Ibn 'Abidin; he would not begin the lesson until he arrived, while the other was with him in utmost politeness and reverence. The lesson of al-Durr was read near the Umayyad Mosque before dawn.
His character and appearance:
The subject of this biography had a good appearance and beautiful praiseworthy character, which made him familiar and beloved to everyone who saw him.
His blessed son, Sayyid Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din Afandi (may Allah have mercy on him) says: "He (may Allah have mercy on him) was tall, well-proportioned in limbs and fingers, white-skinned, black-haired with a little grey; if his grey hairs were counted, they would be few. He had joined eyebrows, with dignity and majesty, a pleasing appearance and freshness, beautiful face, good inner self, his face radiated light, good cheer and companionship. Whoever met him would hardly forget him, due to the sweetness of his speech, his gentleness, and his complete humility in the prescribed manner. He was of great benefit to those who accompanied him, and he enjoyed pleasant conversation. His gathering included etiquette, good speech, and honor for those who came to him from his family, his lovers, his students, and his companions. Everyone who sat with him said to themselves: 'I am dearer to him than his own child.' His gathering was free from obscenity, backbiting, and speaking about what does not concern him. His times were never free from writing, teaching, and reviewing issues. He was truthful in speech, possessed of intuitive faith and Luqman-like wisdom. He was firm in religion, and no blame of a blamer could affect him in matters of Allah. He spoke the truth even before an unjust ruler. The rulers, judges, and politicians were in awe of him. Damascus in his time was the most just of cities, and the Shari'ah had great prestige there; no one dared to oppress anyone or establish a right without a legal basis, nor in most of the nearby cities. For if a judge ruled against someone without legal justification, the one ruled against would bring the judge's document to him, and he would give a fatwa of its nullity and refer the matter back to the judge, who would execute his fatwa. And there was no important or perplexing incident in all the Islamic lands or the rest of Islamic cities or villages but he would be asked for a fatwa regarding it, despite the abundance of senior scholars and muftis in every city. And the bedouin Arabs, when his fatwa reached them, they would not differ regarding it despite their ignorance of the pure Shari'ah. His word was effective, his intercession accepted, and his writings blessed. He never wrote anything for anyone except that he benefited from it, due to the sincerity of his intention, his good inner self, the strength of his certainty, the intensity of his religion, and his firmness in it. (Takmilah Radd al-Muhtar) (6
His habits and ethics:
In this regard, the author's son, the scholar Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din Afandi, member of the scientific society, compiler of the legal journal on the just rulings during the time of the Ottoman Caliphate, says:
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author (likely Ibn 'Abidin or the author of the original text). It begins by detailing his early studies: he memorized important texts (Shatibiyyah, Maydanigah, Jazariyyah) and studied Shafi'i fiqh before being directed by Shaykh Shakir al-Aqqad to convert to the Hanafi madhhab. Under Shaykh al-Aqqad, he studied major Hanafi works such as Multaqa al-Abhar, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Dirayah, al-Hidayah, and later al-Durr al-Mukhtar. His association with Shaykh al-Aqqad lasted seven years, during which he received spiritual training (particularly the Qadiriyya path) and a strong chain of transmission. After al-Aqqad's death, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi took over as his mentor. The description emphasizes the author's excellent character, physical appearance, and piety. His influence was such that his fatwas were accepted across the Islamic world, even by bedouins, and his word was effective with rulers. The passage concludes with a note about the author's habits and ethics, quoting his son. This biography sets the context for the author's authority in Hanafi fiqh and fatwa, reflecting the high standards of learning and conduct expected of a mufti.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-'Allamah): An honorific title for a highly learned scholar, used repeatedly for the author and his teachers.
المذهب الإمام الأعظم (al-madhhab al-imam al-a'zam): The Hanafi madhhab, attributed to Abu Hanifa, who is called the Greatest Imam.
الطريقة القادرية (al-tariqah al-qadiriyyah): A Sufi order attributed to 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, which the author practiced and maintained.
العدالة (al-'adalah): Justice or moral probity; a required condition for a mufti to be accepted as reliable.
الصدع بالحق (al-sada' bi al-haqq): Speaking the truth firmly, especially before authority; a quality of the author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What did the bedouin Arabs do when they received the author's fatwa?
A) They ignored it
B) They disputed it
C) They accepted it without disagreement
D) They asked for clarification

Key Takeaway
A mufti's moral authority—grounded in truthfulness, piety, and fearlessness in speaking the truth—is essential for his fatwas to be accepted and effective.

Life of the Author
beginner
8 min
Mufti Adab from the Author's Biography
Biographical description highlighting mufti adab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the essential personal qualities and practices of a Hanafi mufti as exemplified by the author, and explain how each quality contributes to the reliability and acceptance of his fatwas.

Core Idea
A mufti's authority rests on personal piety, fearless truthfulness, and unimpeachable integrity.

This biographical passage introduces us to the author of Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. Beyond mere facts, his life serves as a practical embodiment of the adab (etiquette) required of a mufti. By examining his character, we learn what it means to be a mufti who commands respect and whose fatwas are accepted without question.

Guided Path
1
Identify Physical and General Demeanor
Read the description of his appearance and manner: tall, handsome, dignified, pleasant speech. These outward qualities reflect the inner state and contribute to the awe (haybah) a mufti should inspire.
2
Extract Qualities Related to Mufti Role
Look for mentions of piety (especially in Hajj), truthfulness, fearlessness in speaking truth to rulers, generosity, and avoidance of dubious financial dealings. Each is a pillar of mufti adab.
3
Analyze Interactions with Rulers and Judges
Note how judges implemented his fatwas and even Bedouins accepted them. This shows the mufti’s authority transcends formal position; it is earned through character.
4
Observe Handling of Financial Matters
Focus on his refusal of a bribe for a weak opinion and his abstinence from purchasing endowed properties with irregularities. A mufti must be scrupulously honest and avoid conflicts of interest.
5
Synthesize into Mufti Adab Guidelines
Combine the observed qualities into a set of practical guidelines for a mufti: piety, truthfulness, fearlessness, generosity, and financial integrity.

العلمية الجمع المجلة الشرعية في الأحكام العدلية في زمن الخلافة العثمانية :

وكان سيدي رحمه الله تعالى ورعًا في سائر أحواله وعلى الخصوص
في حال إحرامه في حجته، فإنه تحرى للطعام غاية التحرى مع قلة تناول الطعام إلا بقدر الضرورة.
وكان رحمه الله تعالى كثير البر والصلة الأرحامه، يواسيهم بأفعاله، وأقواله وماله، وبالخصوص شقيقه العلامة الفاضل الفقيه الصو في التقى الصالح السيد عبد الغنى. وكان يعتنى ويتفرس الخير بأكبر أولاده، وهو العالم العلامة العمدة الفهامة الشيخ السيد أحمد أفندى أمين الفتوى بدمشق حالا، ويهتم بتربيته ويقول لوالده : دع لى من ولدك السيد أحمد وأنا أربيه وأعلمه " . فعلمه القرآن العظيم و أقرأه مسلسلات العلامة ابن عقيلة، وأجازه إجازة عامة حتى صار من أفاضل عصره، وله تأليفات عديدة منها : شرح م ولد ابن حجر، شرحه شرحا لم يسق على سواله، وشرح على علم الحال الذى ألف صاحب السماعة والفضيلة جندى زاده أمين أفندى العباسي رئيس دیوان تمييز ولاية سورية ونشأ له ولدان نجيبان فاضلان: أحدهما: السيد محمد أبو الخير، مسود الفتوى بدمشق، وخطيب جامع برسبايي الشهير بجامع الورد و مدرسه وثانيهما: السيد راغب إمام الجامع المذكور. وكان رحمه الله تعالى حريصًا على إفادة الناس وجبر خواطرهم ، مكرماً للعلماء والأشراف وطلبة العلم، ويواسيهم بماله، وكان كثير التصدق على ذوى الهيئات من الفقراء لا يسألون الناس إلحافًا . وكان غيوراً على أهل العلم والشرف ناصراً لهم دافعا عنهم ما استطاع . وكان مهابا، مطاعاً، نافذ ا الكلمة عند الحكام وأعيان الناس يأكل من مال تجارته بمباشرته شريكه مـدة حياته . وكان رحمه الله تعالى ،ورعا دينا عفيفا، حتى أنه عرض عليه خمسون كيسا من الدراهم لأجل فتوى على قول مرجوح فردها ولم يقبل وقد امتنع عن شراء العقارات الموقوفة التي عليها كدك، أو محاكرة، أو قيمة، أو بالإجارتين . وكان وقف جده لأم أبيه شروطا نظره للأرشد من ذرية
Introduction to the Verification. Biography of the Author. Al-Din Afandi, may Allah have mercy on him: 'He was tall, with handsome limbs and fingers, white-skinned, black-haired with a bit of grey—if his grey hairs were counted, they would be counted... joined eyebrows, possessing awe and dignity, a commendable appearance and freshness, beautiful face, good inner character, his face shining with light, pleasant countenance and companionship. Whoever met him would hardly forget him due to the sweetness of his speech, his gentleness, and his complete humility in the prescribed manner. He was very beneficial to those who accompanied him, and his gatherings included etiquette, good speech, and honoring those who came to him from his family, his loved ones, his students, and his companions. Everyone who sat with him would say to himself: I am dearer to him than his own son. His gathering was free from obscenity, backbiting, and speaking about what does not concern him. His times were never free from writing, teaching, and reviewing issues. He was truthful in speech, possessed intuitive faith and Luqman-like wisdom. Firm in religion, he would not be blamed by any blamer in the matter of Allah. He proclaimed the truth even before a tyrannical ruler. Rulers, judges, and people of politics were in awe of him. Damascus in his time was the most just of cities, and the Sharia had great prestige; no one dared to oppress anyone or to prove a right without a legitimate shar'i basis, and similarly in most nearby cities. For if a judge ruled against someone without a legitimate basis, the one ruled against would come to him with a copy of the judge's proof, and he would issue a fatwa of its invalidity, and then the judge would be referred to, and he would implement his fatwa. And if an important or confusing incident occurred in all other Islamic cities or villages, they would seek his fatwa despite the presence of many senior scholars and muftis in every city. The Bedouin Arabs, when his fatwa reached them, would not differ over it despite their ignorance of the pure Sharia. His word was effective, his intercession accepted, and his writing blessed. He never wrote for anyone but that he benefited from it, due to his sincerity of intention, good character, strong certainty, and his firmness and strength in religion. (Takmila Radd al-Muhtar, 6) His Habits and Character: His son, the scholar Muhammad Alaa al-Din Afandi, member of the Scientific Society that compiled the Sharia Journal on Judicial Verdicts in the time of the Ottoman Caliphate, says: My master, may Allah have mercy on him, was scrupulously pious in all his states, especially in the state of ihram during his Hajj; he was extremely careful about food, eating very little except as needed. He was very generous and maintained family ties, supporting them with his actions, words, and wealth, especially his brother, the virtuous, ascetic, pious scholar Sayyid Abd al-Ghani. He paid attention to and perceived goodness in his eldest son, the scholar, the eminent, the intelligent, the learned, Shaykh Sayyid Ahmad Afandi, currently the Amin al-Fatwa in Damascus, and he was concerned with his upbringing. He said to his father: 'Leave for me your son Sayyid Ahmad; I will raise and teach him.' So he taught him the Great Quran and made him read the chains of the scholar Ibn Aqila, and gave him a general permission (ijaza) until he became one of the most excellent of his time. He has many writings, including: a commentary on... Mawlid of Ibn Hajar, a commentary that was not given its due, and a commentary on 'Ilm al-Hal authored by the owner of the hearing and virtue Jundi Zada Amin Afandi al-Abbasi, head of the Appeal Court of the province of Syria. He had two excellent and virtuous sons: one is Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Khayr, the scribe of fatwa in Damascus and khatib and teacher at the Barsabayi Mosque known as the Rose Mosque; the other is Sayyid Raghib, imam of the aforementioned mosque. He was keen on benefiting people and mending their hearts, honoring scholars, nobles, and students of knowledge, and supporting them with his wealth. He gave much charity to the poor who had dignity and did not beg. He was protective of the people of knowledge and honor, supporting them and defending them as much as he could. He was revered, obeyed, and his word was effective with rulers and notables. He ate from the wealth of his trade through his partner's direct management throughout his life. He was scrupulous, religious, chaste; even when fifty bags of dirhams were offered to him for a fatwa on a weak opinion, he refused and did not accept. He refrained from purchasing endowed properties that had rent (kadak), lease (muhakara), value (qima), or double rent (ijaratayn). The endowment of his grandfather on his paternal grandmother's side had conditions that its supervision be given to the most upright among the descendants.'
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the author of Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, providing insight into his personality, piety, and influence. It describes his physical appearance, his character as a scholar and mufti, his fearlessness in speaking truth to power, and his exceptional reputation such that his fatwas were accepted even by Bedouins. The text emphasizes his scrupulousness in religious matters, his generosity, his dedication to teaching and writing, and his refusal to accept bribes or issue fatwas on weak opinions. This biography serves to establish the author's authority and reliability as a scholar whose works should be taken seriously. It also gives a glimpse into the social and political context of Damascus during his time, where the Sharia was upheld and his fatwas were highly respected.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A non-binding legal opinion issued by a qualified mufti on a matter of sharia.
أمين الفتوى (Amin al-Fatwa): A formal position in the Ottoman judicial system, responsible for issuing fatwas on behalf of the state or assisting the chief mufti.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The author's biography exemplifies that a mufti's authority is built on personal piety, fearless truth, and unimpeachable integrity.

The Mufti's Ethical Conduct: Lessons from the Author's Biography
Biographical sketch of the author's virtues and family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three ethical principles for a mufti from the biography and explain their application in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
A mufti must be a paragon of piety, integrity, and independence, even when pressured by wealth or worldly interests.

The biography of the author of Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti, written by his son, provides a vivid portrait of a scholar who embodied the highest standards of piety and ethical conduct. This lesson extracts key virtues from his life that are directly relevant to the practice of iftaa, serving as a model for muftis today.

Guided Path
1
Identify acts of piety
Look for descriptions of his carefulness in Hajj (extreme caution about food), his nightly Quran recitation for his deceased father, and his refusal to accept gifts from those with ulterior motives.
These show that a mufti's devotion to Allah must permeate all actions.
2
Recognize financial integrity
Note his refusal of a large bribe for a fatwa on a weak opinion, his avoidance of endowed properties with legal complications, and his decline of a trusteeship to avoid conflict of interest.
A mufti must not be swayed by money or personal benefit.
3
Observe dedication to education and family
He personally taught his son, gave him a general ijazah, and ensured his upbringing. He also supported relatives and the poor.
The mufti is a teacher and caregiver in his community.

وكان سيدي رحمه الله تعالى ورعًا في سائر أحواله وعلى الخصوص في حال إحرامه في حجته، فإنه تحرى للطعام غاية التحرى مع قلة تناول الطعام إلا بقدر الضرورة. وكان رحمه الله تعالى كثير البر والصلة الأرحامه، ولدان نجيبان فاضلان: أحدهما: السيد محمد أبو الخير، مسود الفتوى بدمشق، وخطيب جامع برسبايي الشهير بجامع الورد و مدرسه وثانيهما: السيد راغب إمام الجامع المذكور. وكان رحمه الله تعالى حريصًا على إفادة الناس وجبر خواطرهم ، مكرماً للعلماء والأشراف وطلبة العلم، ويواسيهم بماله، وكان كثير التصدق على ذوى الهيئات من الفقراء لا يسألون الناس إلحافًا . وكان غيوراً على أهل العلم والشرف ناصراً لهم دافعا عنهم ما استطاع . وكان مهابا، مطاعاً، نافذ ا الكلمة عند الحكام وأعيان الناس يأكل من مال تجارته بمباشرته شريكه مـدة حياته . وكان رحمه الله تعالى ،ورعا دينا عفيفا، حتى أنه عرض عليه خمسون كيسا من الدراهم لأجل فتوى على قول مرجوح فردها ولم يقبل وقد امتنع عن شراء العقارات الموقوفة التي عليها كدك، أو محاكرة، أو قيمة، أو بالإجارتين . وكان وقف جده لأم أبيه شروطا نظره للأرشد من ذرية الواقف، فامتنع من توليته وسلمه لأخيه . ولم يتفق له قبول هدية من ذي حاجة أو مصلحة . وكان رحمه الله تعالى بارا بوالديه، ومات والده في حياته سنة سبع وثلاثين بعد المائتين والألف، وصار يقرأ كل ليلة عند النوم ما تيسر من القرآن العظيم ويهديه ثوابه مع ما تقبل له من الأعمال حتى رأى والده في النوم بعد شهر من وفاته وقال له : جزاك الله تعالى خيراً يا ولدى على هذه الخيرات التي تهديها إلى في كل ليلة . وكان سيدى رحمه الله تعالى قد عرض عليه شيخه بنته للزواج، فمنعه والده من زواجها وقال له : أخاف عليك من غضب شيخك وعقوقه إن أغضبت ابنته يوماً ما، وهذا مما لا تخلو منه الجبلة الإنسانية غالبا . وكان والده رحمه الله تعالى شفوقاً عليه ويحبه محبة تامة، حتى إنه لما حج سيدى سنة خمس وثلاثين امتنع والده من دخول داره الجوانية مدة غياب سيدى، ولم ينم على فراش تلك المدة، وهي أربعة أشهر، بل بقى نائماً في داره البرانية . وكان رحمه الله تعالى له خيرات عامة منها : تعمير المساجد، وافتقاد الأرامل والفقراء. وكانت تسعى إليه الوزراء، والأمراء، والموالى، والعلماء والمشايخ والكبراء، والفقراء، وذو الحاجات، وعظمت بركته وعم نفعه، وكثر أخذ الناس عنه . وغالب من أخذ عنه وقرأ عليه أكابر الناس وأشرافهم وأجلاء هم من الموالي والعلماء الكبار والمفتين والمدرسين وأصحاب التأليف والمشاهير، وقصده الناس من الأقطار الشاسعة للقراءة عليه والأخذ عنه ". مكانته الروحانية : قال العلامة السيد محمد علاء الدین آفندی رحمه الله تعالى في أوائل تكملة رد المحتار في ترجمة والده مصنف هذا الكتاب : أخذ طريق السادة
My master (may Allah have mercy on him) was pious in all his states, especially during his state of ihram in his Hajj, for he was extremely careful about food, eating little except as necessary. He was abundant in righteousness and maintaining family ties, consoling them with his actions, words, and wealth, especially his brother, the distinguished, virtuous, jurist, pious, righteous Sayyid Abd al-Ghani. He took care and foresaw good in his eldest son, who is the scholar, the learned, the pillar, the very intelligent, Shaykh Sayyid Ahmad Afandi, currently the mufti of Damascus, and he took interest in his upbringing, saying to his father: 'Leave for me from your son Sayyid Ahmad, and I will raise and teach him.' So he taught him the Noble Quran and made him read the chains of transmission of Allamah Ibn Aqila, and gave him a general authorization, until he became among the foremost of his time. He authored many works, including: a commentary on Mawlid Ibn Hajar, a commentary unlike any before; and a commentary on 'Ilm al-Hal authored by the possessor of virtue Jundi Zada Amin Afandi al-Abbasi, head of the Court of Cassation of the province of Syria. He had two excellent, virtuous sons: one is Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Khair, draft fatwa writer in Damascus, khatib of the mosque of Barsbay known as the mosque of al-Ward and its teacher; the second is Sayyid Raghib, imam of the aforementioned mosque. He was eager to benefit people and console their hearts, honoring scholars, nobles, and students of knowledge, and consoling them with his wealth. He gave much charity to the dignified poor who do not importune people. He was protective of the people of knowledge and nobility, supporting them and defending them as much as he could. He was awe-inspiring, obeyed, and his word carried weight with rulers and notables. He ate from the wealth of his business managed by his partner throughout his life. He was pious, religious, and chaste, to the extent that fifty bags of dirhams were offered to him for a fatwa on a weak opinion, but he returned them and did not accept. He refrained from purchasing endowed properties that had any tenant right, lease, value, or double lease. His grandfather from his mother's father had made conditions that the most righteous descendant should oversee his endowment, so he refrained from accepting the trusteeship and handed it over to his brother. He did not happen to accept a gift from anyone in need or with an interest. He was dutiful to his parents; his father died in his lifetime in the year 1237 AH. He would recite whatever was easy from the Noble Quran every night at bedtime and dedicate its reward, along with his accepted deeds, until he saw his father in a dream a month after his death, who said to him: 'May Allah reward you well, my son, for these good deeds you send to me every night.' My master's shaykh offered his daughter in marriage to him, but his father prevented him from marrying her, saying: 'I fear for you the anger and disobedience of your shaykh if you ever anger his daughter, and human nature is rarely free from that.' His father was compassionate towards him and loved him completely, so much so that when my master performed Hajj in the year 1235, his father refrained from entering his inner house during my master's absence, and did not sleep on his bed for that period of four months, but slept in his outer house. He performed general good deeds, including building mosques and caring for widows and the poor. Ministers, princes, judges, scholars, shaykhs, great ones, the poor, and those in need would come to him; his blessing was great, his benefit widespread, and many people learned from him. Most of those who learned from him and read to him were the great people, nobles, and distinguished among judges, senior scholars, muftis, teachers, authors, and famous figures. People came to him from distant regions to read to him and learn from him. His spiritual rank: Allamah Sayyid Muhammad Ala al-Din Afandi (may Allah have mercy on him) said in the beginning of his supplement to Radd al-Muhtar, in the biography of his father, the author of this book: 'He took the path of the masters...'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the author of Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti, written by his son. It details the author's piety, especially during Hajj where he was extremely careful about food. He was known for his generosity to relatives, particularly his brother Sayyid Abd al-Ghani. He personally took charge of educating his eldest son, Sayyid Ahmad, who became the mufti of Damascus, teaching him Quran and giving him a general ijazah. The author authored commentaries, including one on Mawlid Ibn Hajar. He had two distinguished sons: Muhammad Abu al-Khair, who became a fatwa writer and khatib, and Sayyid Raghib, an imam. The author was dedicated to serving people, honoring scholars, and supporting the poor. He refused a large bribe for a fatwa based on a weak opinion, and avoided any involvement with endowed properties that had legal complications. He even declined the trusteeship of his grandfather's waqf to avoid conflict. His father was very protective, refusing to let him marry his shaykh's daughter for fear of marital discord. The author's piety extended to nightly Quran recitation for his deceased father, which his father acknowledged in a dream. After performing Hajj, his father missed him so much he stayed away from his own house for four months. The author's reputation attracted dignitaries and commoners alike, and his spiritual status is affirmed by the commentary of Allamah Sayyid Muhammad Ala al-Din Afandi in the beginning of his supplement to Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
إجازة عامة (ijāzah ʿāmmah): A general authorization given by a scholar to a student to transmit all that the scholar has transmitted, often including a chain of transmission.
مسود الفتوى (musawwid al-fatwā): A person who drafts legal responsa (fatwas) for a mufti, often a senior assistant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The ideal mufti combines deep knowledge with unwavering piety and ethical integrity, as exemplified by the author of this text.

The Mufti's Character and Spiritual Training
Biographical account of the author's character, piety, and teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key biographical elements that establish a Hanafi mufti's authority and evaluate their relevance for fatwa reliability.

Core Idea
A mufti's personal piety and spiritual discipline are integral to the authority of his fatwas.

In the Hanafi tradition, a mufti is not merely a jurist but a person of deep faith and moral integrity. This biographical passage from the introduction to Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti describes the author's character, his respectful relationship with his father and teachers, and his spiritual training. Understanding these qualities helps us appreciate why his legal opinions carried weight and how the tradition links personal virtue to scholarly authority.

Guided Path
1
Extract Qualities of Piety
Identify the specific actions and characteristics that demonstrate the author's piety (e.g., refusing gifts, reciting Quran nightly, charitable works). Note how these reflect on his trustworthiness as a mufti.
2
Analyze Relationships of Adab
Examine the author's interactions with his father and teachers. The story of his father preventing a marriage and the father's extreme love shows the value of filial piety and parental guidance in forming a scholar's character.
3
Identify Spiritual Training
Trace the author's spiritual path: affiliation with the Qadiriyya order, the incident with Sheikh Muhammad 'Abd al-Nabi predicting his future, and receiving a general ijaza. This establishes a chain of blessing and knowledge transmission.
4
Connect to Iftaa Authority
Explain how these biographical details support the reliability of the author's fatwas. A mufti with such piety, adab, and recognized spiritual station is more likely to be a trustworthy transmitter of the madhhab.

الواقف، فامتنع من توليته وسلمه لأخيه . ولم يتفق له قبول هدية من ذي حاجة أو مصلحة .
وكان رحمه الله تعالى بارا بوالديه، ومات والده في حياته سنة سبع وثلاثين بعد المائتين والألف، وصار يقرأ كل ليلة عند النوم ما تيسر من القرآن العظيم ويهديه ثوابه مع ما تقبل له من الأعمال حتى رأى والده في النوم بعد شهر من وفاته وقال له : جزاك الله تعالى خيراً يا ولدى على هذه الخيرات التي تهديها إلى في كل ليلة . وكان سيدى رحمه الله تعالى قد عرض عليه شيخه بنته للزواج، فمنعه والده من زواجها وقال له : أخاف عليك من غضب شيخك وعقوقه إن أغضبت ابنته يوماً ما، وهذا مما لا تخلو منه الجبلة الإنسانية غالبا . وكان والده رحمه الله تعالى شفوقاً عليه ويحبه محبة تامة، حتى إنه لما حج سيدى سنة خمس وثلاثين امتنع والده من دخول داره الجوانية مدة غياب سيدى، ولم ينم على فراش تلك المدة، وهي أربعة أشهر، بل بقى نائماً في داره البرانية . وكان رحمه الله تعالى له خيرات عامة منها : تعمير المساجد، وافتقاد الأرامل والفقراء. وكانت تسعى إليه الوزراء، والأمراء، والموالى، والعلماء والمشايخ والكبراء، والفقراء، وذو الحاجات، وعظمت بركته وعم نفعه، وكثر أخذ الناس عنه . وغالب من أخذ عنه وقرأ عليه أكابر الناس وأشرافهم وأجلاء هم من الموالى والعلماء الكبار والمفتين والمدرسين وأصحاب التأليف والمشاهير، وقصده الناس من الأقطار الشاسعة للقراءة عليه والأخذ عنه .

ترجمة المصنف
القادرية، عن شيخه الشيخ محمد شاكر رحمه الله، حتى أخبر عنه من يوثق بصلاحه ودينه ممن صحبه في سفره من تلامذته : إنى ما وجدته عليه شيئًا يشينه في دنياه ولا في دينه . وكان حسن الأخلاق والسمات، ما سمعنه في سفرى معه في طريق الحج تكلم بكلمة أغاظ يبا أحدا من رفقاءه وخدمه، أو أحداً من الناس أجمعين . اللهم إلا إن رأى منكراً فيغيره من ساعته على مقتضى الشريعة المطهرة العادلة . وكانت ترد إليه الأسئلة من غالب البلاد و انتفع به خلق كثير من حاضر وباد .
وكان سيدي رحمه الله تعالى ذهب مرةً مع شيخه السيد محمد شاكر لزيارة بعض علماء الهند وصلحاءها الشيخ محمد عبد النبي لما ورد دمشق ، فلما دخلا علیه جلس شیخ سیدی و بقی سیدی واقفا في العتبة بين يدى شیخه حاملا نعله بيده كما هو عادته مع شيخه، فقال الشيخ محمد عبد النبي لشيخ سيدى "مر هذا الغلام السيد فليجلس ، فإني لا أجلس حتى يجلس ؛ فإنه ستقبل يده وينتفع بفضله في سائر البلاد وعليه نور آل بيت النبوة " فقال له الشيخ محمد شاکر اجلس يا ولدى وكذلك وقع له مع شيخه المذكور إشارة نظير هذه من الإمام الصوفى الشهير والولي الكبير الشيخ طه الكردي قدس سره. ومن ذاك الوقت زاد اعتناء الشيخ به والتفاته إليه بالتعليم .
وكان شيخه المذكور كثيراً ما يأخذه معه ويحضره دروس أشياخه، حتى إنه أخذه وأحضره درس شيخه العلامة العامل، الولى ، الصالح، شيخ الحديث الشيخ محمد الكزبرى ، واستجلاء له فأجازه وكتب له إجازة عامة على ظهر ثبته مؤرخة فى افتتاح ليلة غيرة منة عشرة ومائتين وألف و ترجمه سید از شوم في ثبته ترجمه انسته ورثاه أيضا سيدي عند وفاته ليلة الجمعة لتسع عشرة لينة خلت من ربيع الأول سنة مجدى وعشرين ومائتين، وألف بقصيدة مؤرخاً وفاته فيها .
Introduction to the Investigation
11
Biography of the Author
... (the author) refused to be appointed (as trustee) and handed it over to his brother. He never accepted a gift from someone in need or with a vested interest. He was, may Allah have mercy on him, dutiful to his parents. His father died during his lifetime in the year 1237 AH. He began to recite every night before sleep whatever was easy from the Great Quran and gift its reward along with his other accepted deeds. Until he saw his father in a dream a month after his death, and his father said to him: 'May Allah reward you well, my son, for these good deeds you send to me every night.' My master, may Allah have mercy on him, was offered his teacher's daughter in marriage, but his father prevented him from marrying her, saying: 'I fear for you from your teacher's anger and disobedience if you ever anger his daughter, which human nature is not free from often.' And his father, may Allah have mercy on him, was affectionate towards him and loved him completely, so much so that when my master performed Hajj in the year 1235 AH, his father refrained from entering his inner house during my master's absence, and did not sleep on his bed for that period of four months, but remained sleeping in his outer house. He, may Allah have mercy on him, had many charitable works, including building mosques and caring for widows and the poor. Ministers, princes, masters, scholars, sheikhs, elders, poor people, and those in need used to come to him. His blessing was great, his benefit widespread, and many people learned from him. Most of those who learned from him and read under him were the elite, nobles, and dignitaries among the masters, great scholars, muftis, teachers, authors, and celebrities. People came to him from distant lands to read under him and learn from him.
His Spiritual Station:
The scholar Sayyid Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din Afandi, may Allah have mercy on him, said at the beginning of the completion of Radd al-Muhtar in the biography of his father, the author of this book: He took the path of the Qadiriyya order from his teacher Sheikh Muhammad Shakir, may Allah have mercy on him, to the extent that one of his trustworthy and religious students who accompanied him on a journey reported: 'I never found anything in him that would disgrace him in this world or his religion.' He had good character and qualities. I never heard him, during my journey with him on the Hajj road, say a word that would anger any of his companions or servants, or any person at all, unless he saw a wrong, then he would change it immediately according to the pure and just Sharia. Questions used to come to him from most countries, and many people, both present and absent, benefited from him.
My master, may Allah have mercy on him, once went with his teacher Sayyid Muhammad Shakir to visit some scholars and righteous people of India, Sheikh Muhammad 'Abd al-Nabi, when he came to Damascus. When they entered upon him, my master's teacher sat down while my master remained standing at the threshold before his teacher, carrying his sandals in his hand as was his custom with his teacher. Sheikh Muhammad 'Abd al-Nabi said to my master's teacher: 'Tell this sayyid youth to sit, for I will not sit until he sits; because his hand will be kissed and people will benefit from his virtue in all countries, and upon him is the light of the household of prophethood.' So Sheikh Muhammad Shakir said to him: 'Sit, my son.' A similar indication occurred with the aforementioned teacher from the famous Sufi Imam and great saint Sheikh Tah al-Kurdi, may Allah sanctify his secret. From that time on, the teacher's care and attention towards him increased in teaching.
His aforementioned teacher often took him with him and made him attend the lessons of his own teachers, until he took him and made him attend the lesson of his teacher, the righteous scholar, the saint, the hadith scholar Sheikh Muhammad al-Kuzbari, and he (the sheikh) admired him, so he gave him a general ijaza written on the back of his thabat, dated the night of the 10th of Muharram 1210 AH. And he (Sayyid 'Ala' al-Din) also mentioned him in his thabat with a biography that pleased him. And my master also composed a eulogy for him upon his death on Friday night, the 19th of Rabi' al-Awwal 1220 AH, with a poem dating his death.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the author of Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, taken from the editor's introduction (taḥqīq). It highlights the author's piety, his deep respect for his father and teachers, and his widespread acceptance as a scholar. The text narrates that the author's father prevented him from marrying his teacher's daughter out of fear that any marital discord might offend the teacher. Despite this, the father's love was immense, as shown by his refraining from using the inner house and bed during the author's Hajj journey. The author's charitable activities included mosque construction and care for the needy. His spiritual station is attested by a story where a visiting scholar recognized his future prominence and insisted he sit. The author belonged to the Qadiriyya order and received an ijaza from Sheikh Muhammad al-Kuzbari. The passage gives us insight into the character of a great Hanafi jurist and the environment in which he was raised—one of strict adab (etiquette) towards elders and deep spiritual training.

Key Terms
القادرية (al-Qadiriyya): A Sufi order (tariqa) attributed to 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani; the author took this path from his teacher.
إجازة عامة (ijaza 'amma): A general license to transmit hadith or teach, given by a scholar to a student.
آل بيت النبوة (Al Bayt al-Nubuwwa): The household of prophethood, i.e., the family of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The author was already married.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's authority is strengthened by his piety, adab, and recognized chain of spiritual and scholarly transmission.

The Role of Ijāzah in Hanafī Knowledge Transmission
Narrative of the author's acquisition of ijāzāt from his teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of ijāzat 'āmma (general permission) and identify its significance in the Hanafī tradition of knowledge transmission as illustrated by the author's life.

Core Idea
Ijāzah connects teacher and student, ensuring authority and continuity of the Hanafī tradition.

This biographical passage highlights several instances where the author received general permissions (ijāzāt 'āmma) from his shaykhs. These permissions were not mere certificates; they were formal authorizations to transmit the shaykh's knowledge and works. Understanding ijāzah is essential for grasping how Hanafī scholarship was preserved and disseminated across generations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of permissions mentioned
Look for the phrase 'ijāzat 'āmma' in the text and note who granted them and when.
The author received multiple general permissions from different shaykhs.
2
Understand the significance of the thabit
The permissions were written on the back of the shaykhs' registers (thabit), indicating a formal documentation process.
The thabit is a collection of a shaykh's works, teachers, and authorizations.
3
Analyze the chain of authorization
Trace how the author's shaykh introduced him to other scholars, who then granted him permission, showing the network of knowledge transmission.
This reflects the Hanafī emphasis on continuous chains (sanad).
4
Apply the concept to modern fatwa practice
Consider how the need for authorization continues today in the form of formal permission to issue fatwas.
The mufti today is expected to have clear authorization from recognized scholars.

القادرية، عن شيخه الشيخ محمد شاكر رحمه الله، حتى أخبر عنه من يوثق بصلاحه ودينه ممن صحبه في سفره من تلامذته : إنى ما وجدته عليه شيئًا يشينه في دنياه ولا في دينه . وكان حسن الأخلاق والسمات، ما سمعنه في سفرى معه في طريق الحج تكلم بكلمة أغاظ يبا أحدا من رفقاءه وخدمه، أو أحداً من الناس أجمعين . اللهم إلا إن رأى منكراً فيغيره من ساعته على مقتضى الشريعة المطهرة العادلة . وكانت ترد إليه الأسئلة من غالب البلاد و انتفع به خلق كثير من حاضر وباد .
وكان سيدي رحمه الله تعالى ذهب مرةً مع شيخه السيد محمد شاكر لزيارة بعض علماء الهند وصلحاءها الشيخ محمد عبد النبي لما ورد دمشق ، فلما دخلا علیه جلس شیخ سیدی و بقی سیدی واقفا في العتبة بين يدى شیخه حاملا نعله بيده كما هو عادته مع شيخه، فقال الشيخ محمد عبد النبي لشيخ سيدى "مر هذا الغلام السيد فليجلس ، فإني لا أجلس حتى يجلس ؛ فإنه ستقبل يده وينتفع بفضله في سائر البلاد وعليه نور آل بيت النبوة " فقال له الشيخ محمد شاکر اجلس يا ولدى وكذلك وقع له مع شيخه المذكور إشارة نظير هذه من الإمام الصوفى الشهير والولي الكبير الشيخ طه الكردي قدس سره. ومن ذاك الوقت زاد اعتناء الشيخ به والتفاته إليه بالتعليم .
وكان شيخه المذكور كثيراً ما يأخذه معه ويحضره دروس أشياخه، حتى إنه أخذه وأحضره درس شيخه العلامة العامل، الولى ، الصالح، شيخ الحديث الشيخ محمد الكزبرى ، واستجلى له فأجازه وكتب له إجازة عامة على ظهر ثبته مؤرخة فى افتتاح ليلة غرة منة عشرة ومائتين وألف و ترجمه سيد از شوم في ثبته ترجمه انسته ورثاه أيضا سيدي عند وفاته ليلة الجمعة لتسع عشرة ليلة خلت من ربيع الأول سنة مجدى وعشرين ومائتين، وألف بقصيدة مؤرخاً وفاته فيها .
