فهرس مؤلفاته : ترك العلامة المترجم كثيراً من المصنفات القيمة، والعديد من الرسائل النافعة التي تشهد بعلو قدره وباهر تحقيقه وهى ۱ - الحاشية رد المحتار على الدر المختار " وهى عمدة المذهب الحنفى، وأعظم كتبه المتداولة ، وقد طبعت طبعات كثيرة أرقاها : طبعة بولاق سنة ١٢٧٢هـ في خمسة مجلدات، ثم سنة ١٢٧٦ ، ثم سنة ۱۲۹۹ . ثم في المطبعة الميمنية ۱۳۰۷ ، وكذا في إستنبول ۱۳۰۷ ، ثم بالميمنية أيضا ۱۳۲۳ . ثم بمطبعة البابي الحلبى فى ثمانية مجلدات مع التكملة. ثم بإستنبول، وصورت مراراً . ۲- منحة الخالق : هى حواش علّقها أولا على هامش صفحاتها، ثم جمعها، ولم يتعرض فيها غالباً إلا لما فيه إيضاح أو تقوية، أو لما فيه بحث أو إشكال إلا في بعض المواضع التي تحتاج إلى تحرير من النهر الفائق " لعمر ابن نجيم . وبعض ما كتبه الشيخ خير الدين ،الرملى، وسمى ذلك به منحة الخالق على البحر الرائق". هذا وقد أتم ابن عابدين شرح ابن نجيم الذي وصل فيه إلى الإجارة الفاسدة، وقد تم طبع الكتاب على هامش الشرخ في سبعة مجلدات والثامن تكملة البحر" للطورى سنة ١٣١١ بالمطبعة العلمية بمصر . - العقود الدرية في تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية : وهي تنقيح الفتاوى العلامة حامد الدين العمادی، طبعت في مجلدين وصور عنها . ٤ - حاشية على شرح ملتقى الأبحر للحصكفى . ٥- حاشية على تفسير القاضي البيضاوي : التزم فيها ألا يذكر شيئًا مما ذكره المفسرون قبله . ٦ - حاشية على "إفاضة الأنوار " شرح المنار للحصكفى : وهي غير نسمات الأسحار الآتية. -٧- حاشية على شرح " التقرير والتحبير " في الأصول لابن أمير حاج. - حاشية سمّاها "رفع الأنظار عما أورده الحلبي على الدر المختار " . ۹ - حاشية على شرح المنار للعلائي المسماة نسمات الأسحار على إفاضة الأنوار " طبعت مرتين . ١٠- حاشية على "المطول " في البلاغة . ۱۱ - حاشية "فتح رب الأرباب على لب الألباب شرح نبذة الأعراب لابن هشام مخطوط في الظاهرية . ۱۲ - الدرر المضيئة في شرح نظم الأبحر الشعرية . ١٣ - فتاوى في الفقه الحنفى وهى تقرب من مائة غير الرسالة المعروفة "أجوبة محققة " . - ١٤ - شرح الكافى فى العروض والقوافي . ١٥ - ذیل سلك الدرر للمرادى . ١٦ - مجموع النفائس والنوادر . -۱۷ قصة المولد النبوى الشريف .
Index of his works: The translated scholar left many valuable writings and numerous beneficial treatises that testify to his high rank and brilliant verification. They are: 1- al-Hashiyah Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, which is the foundation of the Hanafi school and the greatest of his circulated books. It has been printed many times, the best being the Bulaq edition in 1272 AH in five volumes, then 1276, then 1299. Then in al-Maymaniyyah press 1307, also in Istanbul 1307, then again al-Maymaniyyah 1323. Then in al-Babi al-Halabi press in eight volumes with the supplement. Then in Istanbul, and reprinted many times. 2- Minhat al-Khaliq: It is glosses he first wrote on the margins of its pages, then collected them. In it he mostly only discusses what requires clarification or strengthening, or what involves discussion or difficulty, except for some places that needed editing from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq by Umar Ibn Nujaym and some of what Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli wrote. He named it Minhat al-Khaliq ala al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Ibn Abidin completed Ibn Nujaym's commentary which reached to invalid lease (ijarah fasidah). The book was printed as a margin on the commentary [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq] in seven volumes, the eighth being Takmilat al-Bahr by al-Turi in 1311 at the Scientific Press in Egypt. 3- al-Uqud al-Durriyyah fi Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyyah: This is a revision of the fatwas of al-Allamah Hamid al-Din al-Amadi; printed in two volumes and reproduced. 4- Hashiyah ala Sharh Multaqa al-Abhar li al-Haskafi. 5- Hashiyah ala Tafsir al-Qadi al-Baydawi: He committed in it to not mention anything that previous exegetes mentioned. 6- Hashiyah ala Ifadat al-Anwar Sharh al-Manar li al-Haskafi: It is not the same as Nasamat al-Ashar below. 7- Hashiyah ala Sharh al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir fi al-Usul li Ibn Amir Hajj. 8- Hashiyah named Raf' al-Anzar 'amma Aradahu al-Halabi ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar. 9- Hashiyah ala Sharh al-Manar li al-Alla'i called Nasamat al-Ashar ala Ifadat al-Anwar; printed twice. 10- Hashiyah ala al-Mutawwal fi al-Balaghah. 11- Hashiyah Fath Rabb al-Arbab ala Lub al-Albab Sharh Nubdhat al-A'rab li Ibn Hisham; manuscript in al-Zahiriyyah. 12- al-Durar al-Madiyyah fi Sharh Nazm al-Abhur al-Shi'riyyah. 13- Fatawa fi al-Fiqh al-Hanafi, close to one hundred, excluding the known treatise 'Ajwibah Muhqqqaqah. 14- Sharh al-Kafi fi al-Arud wa al-Qawafi. 15- Dhayl Silk al-Durar li al-Muradi. 16- Majmu' al-Nafa'is wa al-Nawadir. 17- Qissat al-Mawlid al-Nabawi al-Sharif.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of Ibn Abidin's works, compiled by the editor of the book. Ibn Abidin (d. 1252 AH) is one of the greatest late Hanafi jurists; his Radd al-Muhtar is the foremost reference for fatwa in the Hanafi school. The list records 17 works spanning fiqh, usul, tafsir, Arabic grammar, poetry, and biography. Notable is his Minhat al-Khaliq, a gloss on al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym. The list also includes lesser-known works like a poem on prophethood. The passage emphasizes his prolific output and the value of his scholarly contributions.

Key Terms
الحاشية رد المحتار على الدر المختار (al-Hashiyah Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar): Ibn Abidin's magnum opus, the most authoritative Hanafi fatwa compendium
منحة الخالق (Minhat al-Khaliq): Gloss by Ibn Abidin on al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, focusing on problematic points
العقود الدرية في تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية (al-Uqud al-Durriyyah fi Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyyah): Revision of the fatwas of Hamid al-Din al-Amadi, a Hanafi jurist

The Author's Works and His Masterpiece on Mufti Methodology
Listing the works of the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major works of the author and identify the one most relevant to Usul al-Iftaa.

Core Idea
The author's commentary on his own poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' is the key text for mufti methodology.

This passage lists over twenty works by the author of this commentary, spanning fiqh, usul, rhetoric, and more. Among them, the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' is central to our study, outlining the rules every mufti must know. This lesson surveys his output to contextualize his authority.

Guided Path
1
Scan the List of Works
Quickly read through the enumerated works from 1 to 24, noting the variety of subjects: fiqh, usul, tafsir, Arabic language, and even medical topics.
This is a memorization anchor; the list is not exhaustive but representative of his scholarly breadth.
2
Identify the Core Work for This Course
Locate item 20: 'Sharh Manzumah Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' – a commentary on his own 74-line poem on the rules of issuing fatwas. This is the primary text for our study.
The poem itself is entitled 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' and the commentary is the current text.
3
Recognize the Author's Methodological Signature
Notice that in his gloss on Tafsir al-Baydawi, he committed to not repeating earlier exegetes, indicating a preference for original contributions. This reflects his approach in other works.
Understanding his method helps appreciate the value he placed on adding new insights.

21 - 'Al-Fawa'id al-Mukhtassa bi-Ahkam Kayy al-Himma': It is a medical issue, invented by one of the skilled physicians to extract pus from a boil using a chickpea. The author compiled in it the results of two treatises: one by Allama al-Sharnablali named 'Al-Ahkam al-Mulakhkhas fi Hukm Ma' al-Himma', and the second by Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi named 'Al-Abhath al-Mulakhkhas fi Hukm Kayy al-Himma'. He added the opinion of the school's scholars. He finished drafting it at the end of Rajab 1227 AH.
22 - 'Manhal al-Waridin min Bihar al-Fayd 'ala Dhikr al-Muta'ahilin': It is a commentary on the treatise 'Dhikr al-Muta'ahilin' by al-Barkawi, author of 'al-Tariqa al-Muhammadiyya', concerning what women are afflicted with regarding menstruation, postpartum bleeding, istihada, rulings, and other matters. The commentary was completed on the 27th of Dhu al-Qa'dah 1241 AH.
23 - 'Raf' al-Taraddud fi 'Aqd al-Asabi' 'inda al-Tashahhud': In it he collected the statements of our imams regarding pointing the index finger and bending the fingers during tashahhud, when some jurists of his time only pointed without bending the fingers. He completed it in Rajab 1236 AH. Then he appended a further supplement when he saw a treatise by Mulla 'Ali al-Qari that favored the narration of pointing without bending. He completed that supplement in Rabi' al-Awwal 1249 AH.

This passage is a biographical list of the works of the author (المصنف) of this commentary. The list includes a variety of books on fiqh, usul, Arabic language, and more. Notably, item 20 is 'Sharh Manzumat Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', a commentary on his own poem of 74 lines on the rules of mufti conduct. Other works include fatwa collections, commentaries on Hidayah, and legal treatises. Parsing the Author's Bibliography: Types of Hanafi Fatwa Works
Listing the author's works with brief descriptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a Hanafi mufti's works by genre (sharh, risalah, etc.) and identify which kinds of writings are essential for usul al-iftaa.

Core Idea
A mufti's bibliography reveals how legal theory meets practice through commentaries, treatises, and refutations.

This passage lists the works of a Hanafi scholar, most likely the author of the book you are studying. It is not a legal ruling but a scholarly biography that shows the range of issues a mufti engaged with. Understanding these genres helps you appreciate how Hanafi jurists produced fatwa-related literature—commentaries on core texts, treatises on novel medical/legal issues, refutations of popular innovations, and responses to specific fatwa requests. As a future mufti, recognizing the purpose and structure of these works is part of your training.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his role
Who is the muṣannif? Likely a Hanafi scholar from the 13th century AH. He is the compiler of the book and the subject of this biography.
2
Scan the list for different genres
Look for shurūḥ (commentaries), rasāʾil (treatises), and responses to specific issues (fatāwā). Examples: 'Sharḥ ʿUqūd Rasm al-Muftī' is a commentary; 'al-ʿIlm al-Ẓāhir' is a treatise; 'al-Ibānah' is a fatwa response.
Each title often indicates the genre.
3
Note the topics covered
Topics range from jurisprudence (poetic version of al-Kanz) to medical issues (cauterization with chickpea), to contemporary debates (bequests for recitations, proof of Ramadan crescent). This shows the breadth of a mufti's concerns.
Some works address emerging issues like the plague in Damascus.
4
Link each work to a function in iftāʾ
Some works clarify rules for the mufti himself (e.g., sharḥ of rasm al-muftī); some provide guidance on specific cases (e.g., payment for custody); some refute incorrect practices (e.g., bequests for recitations).
The work on the finger position during tashahhud resolves a contemporary dispute.
5
Conclude the significance for usul al-iftaa
A well-versed mufti must be aware of such works for authoritative fatwa. This bibliography serves as a model of how a Hanafi scholar engages with fiqh issues across different contexts.
The author's engagement with both classical texts and novel issues reflects the dynamic nature of ijtihad and iftaa.

۱۸ - نظم الكنز للنسفى : وهو في ثمان مائة بيت، لم يكمله . ۱۹ - العلم الظاهر فى نفع النسب الطاهر : وهي رسالة ألفها تحريراً لمبحث انتفاع النسيب من نسبه إلى سيدنا رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وآله . وسلّم أو عدم ذلك ۲۰ - شرح منظومة عقود رسم المفتى له : شرح بها منظومته في عقود رسم المفتى " ، وما يجب أن يعلمه العالم والمفتي، وهي في أربعة وسبعين بيتا من بحر الرجز . أتم الشرح في شهر ربيع الثاني سنة ١٢٤٣هـ . ۲۱ - الفوائد المخصصة بأحكام كي الحمصة : وهي مسألة طبية، اخترعها أحد حذاق الأطباء ؛ لاستخراج القيح من الدمل بواسطة حمصة، وقد جمع المصنف فيها حاصل رسالتين : إحداهما : للعلامة الشرنبلالي واسمها " الأحكام الملخّصة في حكم ماء الحمصة". والثانية : للشيخ عبد الغني النابلسي، واسمها "الأبحاث الملخصة في حكم كي الحمصة". وضم إلى ذلك قول علماء المذهب. وقد فرغ من تسویدها سلخ رجب سنة ١٢٢٧هـ. -۲۲ - منهل الواردين من بحار الفيض على ذخر المتأهلين : وهي شرح لرسالة ذخر المتأهلين للبركوى صاحب الطريقة المحمدية " فيما ابتليت به النساء من حيض ونفاس، واستحاضة، وأحكام وغير ذلك . وقد تم الفراغ من شرحها السابع والعشرين من ذي القعدة سنة ١٢٤١
٢٣ - رفع التردّد في عقد الأصابع عند التشهد : جمع فيها أقوال أئمتنا في الإشارة بالسبابة، وعقد الأصابع في التشهد حين اقتصر بعض فقهاء عصره على الإشارة بلا عقد للأصابع. وأتمها في رجب من سنة ١٢٣٦هـ . ثم عقبها بتتمة أخرى حين رأى رسالة للملا على القارى، رجح فيها رواية الإشارة بلا عقد . وأتمها في ربيع الأول سنة ١٢٤٩هـ. ٢٤ - تنبيه ذوى الأفهام على أحكام التبليغ خلف الإمام: بين فيها

Introduction to the Investigation
21
Biography of the Author
18 - The Poetic Version of al-Kanz for al-Nasafi: It consists of eight hundred verses, which he did not complete. 19 - The Apparent Knowledge Regarding the Benefit of the Pure Lineage: A treatise he wrote to clarify the discussion of the one related benefiting from his lineage to our master the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, or not. 20 - Commentary on the Poem "Uqud Rasm al-Mufti": He commented on his own poem on the bonds of the mufti's rule and what the scholar and mufti must know. It consists of seventy-four verses in rajaz meter. He completed the commentary in the month of Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1243 AH. 21 - The Special Benefits Regarding the Rulings of Cauterization of the Chickpea: A medical issue, invented by one of the skilled physicians to extract pus from a boil using a chickpea. The author compiled in it the content of two treatises: one by al-Allamah al-Shurunbulali, titled "The Summarized Rulings on the Ruling of Chickpea Water"; the second by Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi, titled "The Summary of Researches on the Ruling of Cauterization of the Chickpea". He added to that the statements of the scholars of the madhhab. He finished drafting it at the end of Rajab 1227 AH. 22 - The Spring of the Arriving Ones from the Seas of Overflow on the "Treasure of the Married": A commentary on the treatise "Treasure of the Married" by al-Birkawi, author of al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah, concerning what women are afflicted with regarding menses, postpartum bleeding, istihadah, rulings, and other matters. The commentary was completed on the 27th of Dhu al-Qa'dah 1241 AH.
23 - Removing Hesitation Regarding Folding the Fingers During Tashahhud: He collected in it the statements of our imams on pointing with the index finger and folding the fingers during tashahhud, when some jurists of his time confined themselves to pointing without folding the fingers. He completed it in Rajab 1236 AH. Then he appended a supplement after seeing a treatise by Mulla Ali al-Qari, in which he gave preponderance to the narration of pointing without folding. He completed it in Rabi' al-Awwal 1249 AH. 24 - Alerting the Possessors of Understanding to the Rulings of Conveying Behind the Imam: He explained in it the rulings of conveying behind the imam in his clear and evident scientific style. He organized it into an introduction, a purpose, and a conclusion. He completed it at the beginning of Muharram 1226 AH.
25 - The Cure for the Ill and Quenching the Thirst Regarding the Ruling of Bequeathing for Qur'an Recitations and Tahleel: He wrote it as a refutation of what had become common practice among people when the plague occurred in Damascus in 1228 and 1229, regarding bequests for recitations and tahleel and other things, with their belief that they are acts of devotion. He swore by Allah that whoever sees it should give it its due; otherwise, he would make his Lord an opponent against him. Then many scholars approved it. He completed it in Rajab 1229.
26 - The Munificent Gift for Explaining Remission of What is on the Obligation, Whether Little or Much: By Ala al-Din...
27 - Alerting the Neglectful and the Drowsy to the Rulings of the Crescent of Ramadan: He collected it in compliance with the order of one of his shaykhs to clarify a legal issue that caused turmoil in Damascus due to an incident that occurred regarding the correctness of proving the crescent of Ramadan in the year 1240 AH. He recorded in it the positions of the four imams. He completed it in Shawwal of that year.
28 - Enriching the Intelligent and Astute in Answering What the Jurist Says: He wrote it to explain the meaning of these two verses: "What does the jurist say, may Allah support him, and may His favor never cease with him, regarding a young man who made divorce conditional on a month before the previous month, which was Ramadan?" The second verse admits eight possible faces, which he explained, then he composed the answer. 29 - The Clarification Regarding Taking Payment for Custody: He wrote it in response to a fatwa incident. 30 - Refining Statements on Maintenance of Offspring and Parents: He intended in compiling it to clarify the principles and rules that facilitate the learner's understanding of these precise issues without falling into error and illusion. He completed it in Shawwal 1235. 31 - Removing Objection and Rebutting Opposition to Their Statement: "Oaths are based on wording, not on intentions": He explained in it their intended meaning of building oaths on wording.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing from the introduction (مقدمة التحقيق) of the book, presenting the author's works with brief descriptions. It is not a legal ruling but rather a scholarly bibliography. The author, identified as the مصنف (compiler/author), was a Hanafi jurist who wrote extensively on diverse subjects: jurisprudence, usul, medicine, and refutations of contemporary practices. The works listed include a commentary on his own poem on the rules of issuing fatwas (شرح عقود رسم المفتى), treatises on medical issues (فوائد الحمصة), family law (منهل الواردين on menstruation and postpartum rulings), a work on the finger position during tashahhud (رفع التردد), a work on conveying behind the imam (تنبيه ذوي الأفهام), a refutation of bequests for Quran recitations (شفاء العليل), a work on proof of the Ramadan crescent (تنبيه الغافل), a work answering a question about conditional divorce (اتحاف الذكى), a work on payment for custody (الإبانة), a work on maintenance of relatives (تحرير النقول), and a work on oaths (رفع الانتقاض). Notably, the author engaged with contemporary issues and sometimes responded to specific fatwa requests. This passage is valuable for understanding the scholarly context and the range of fiqh issues addressed by Hanafi scholars of that period.

Key Terms
المصنف (al-musannif): The author/compiler of the book being introduced, i.e., the Hanafi scholar whose works are listed.
رسالة (risalah): A treatise or monograph on a specific topic, often responding to a particular question or addressing a novel issue.
شرح (sharh): A commentary explaining an earlier text (the matn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which work by the author specifically addresses the issue of pointing the index finger during tashahhud?
A) منهل الواردين
B) رفع التردّد في عقد الأصابع عند التشهد
C) شفاء العليل وبل الغليل
D) تنبيه ذوى الأفهام

Key Takeaway
A mufti's bibliography is a repository of his engagement with fiqh issues; each work reflects a specific need in iftāʾ practice.

The Mufti's Bibliography: A Window into Hanafi Fatwa Practice
List of the author's scholarly works with descriptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of fatwa works authored by a Hanafi mufti and explain how each work serves the purpose of ifta'.

Core Idea
A mufti's writings are direct responses to the legal needs of his community, not mere academic exercises.

This passage lists the scholarly works of a Hanafi mufti, each composed to address specific legal questions or controversies in his time—ranging from bequests during plagues to the sighting of the Ramadan crescent. Understanding these works gives insight into the practice of ifta' in the late Ottoman period and the mufti's role in guiding the community according to Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list and identify the range of topics
Quickly review the titles (25–36) and note the variety: ibadat, muamalat, family law, etc.
This shows the mufti's comprehensive expertise.
2
For each work, determine the occasion or problem that prompted its writing
Read the description to see if it was a response to a question, a refutation of a prevailing practice, or a clarification of a legal issue.
The mufti wrote reactively to community needs.
3
Recognize the structure of each work
Note whether it is a risala (treatise), a sharh (commentary), or a tahqiq (verification).
This indicates the depth of analysis.
4
Reflect on how these works demonstrate the mufti's methodology in applying Hanafi principles
Consider how the author uses Hanafi primary texts, cites authorities, and resolves disputes.
Each work is a practical application of usul al-fiqh.

ترجمة المصنف
موضحا تلك القاعدة بما يتعلق بالأيمان. فرغ من تحريرها في ربيع الثاني
سنة۱۲۳۸
•
-۳۲ رفع الاشتباه عن عبارة الأشباه : وهي عبارة عن شرح لعبارة في " الأشباه والنظائر " لابن نجيم حول معصية الأنبياء، وتحرير تلك المسألة. جمعها امتثالا لأمر شيخه العقاد إذ أحال الجواب إليه . وأتمها في رمضان
سنة۱۲۱۸.
٣٣- تنبيه الولاة والحكام على أحكام شاتم خير الأنام، أو أحد أصحابه الأعلام عليه وعليهم الصلاة والسلام : وهي رسالة ألفها جواباً للشيخ عبدالستار الأتاسي مفتى حمص، وقتها حين اطلع على كلامه في تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية في حكم ساب الخلق صلى الله تعالى عليه وآله وسلّم. ثم ضم إليها أحكام شاتم أحد أصحابه الكرام. وفرغ من تحريرها في جمادى الأولى سنة ١٢٣٧هـ. فجاءت هذه الرسالة تحريراً لتلك المسألة، وتحقيقا
لأحكامها.
٣٤- الأقوال الواضحة الجلية : وهى شرح وتوضيح المسألة ذكرها عن السبكي في "الأشباه " حول نقض القسمة . وقد استوعب معظم هذه الرسالة في حاشيته على "الأشباه ١٥٠-١٧٦ . ثم عزا إلى تنقيح الفتاوى الحامدية . ٣٥- العقود الدرية في قول الواقف : " على الفريضة الشرعية " : جواب لسؤال عن المراد بالفريضة الشرعية في قسم ربع الوقف على مستحقيه على الفريضة الشرعية وهي تلخيص مع تحقيق للرسالة المرضية للعلامة ابن المنقار . فرغ من تصنيفها حدود سنة ١٢٣٠ . ٣٦ - غاية المطلب في اشتراط الواقف عود النصيب إلى أهل الدرجة الأقرب فالأقرب : جواب السؤال . ورد إليه من طرابلس الشام مع بعض الفتاوى . فكانت هذه الرسالة تحقيقا لتلك الفتاوى، وتمحيصاً لهاتيك المسألة
أتمها سيئة ١٢٤٩هـ .
Introduction to the Investigation
22
Biography of the Author
"Ahkam al-Tabligh Khalf al-Imam" in his clear and obvious scientific style, and he arranged it with an introduction, a purpose, and a conclusion. He completed it at the beginning of Muharram in the year 1226.
Jismiyya
-25 "Shifa' al-'Alil wa Ball al-Ghalil fi Hukm al-Wasiyya bi'l-Khatamat wa'l-Tahlil": He wrote it as a refutation of what was prevalent among people when the plague occurred in Damascus in 1228 and 1229 regarding bequests for completing Quran recitations and saying 'La ilaha illa Allah', and other things, with their belief that they are acts of devotion. And he swore by God that whoever sees it should be fair to it, otherwise he has made his Lord an opponent against him. Then many scholars praised it. He completed it in Rajab 1229.
Ad-din
.
26 - "Minhah al-Jalil li-Bayan Isqat ma 'ala al-Dhimmah min Qalil wa Kathir": by 'Ala'
-27 "Tanbih al-Ghafil wa'l-Wasnan 'ala Ahkam Hilal Ramadan": He compiled it in compliance with the order of one of his teachers to write a legal issue about which Damascus was in turmoil; due to a major incident regarding the validity of proving the crescent of Ramadan in the year 1240 AH. He recorded in it the opinions of the four Imams. He completed it in Shawwal of that year.
28 - "Ithaf al-Dhaki al-Nabih fi Jawab ma Yaqul al-Faqih": He wrote it to explain the meaning of these two verses: "What does the faqih say, may God support him and his excellence never cease?" about a young man who made divorce conditional on a month before what comes after it, Ramadan. Considering that the second verse has eight possible meanings, he explained them and then composed the answer.
-29 - "al-Ibanah 'an Akhdh al-Ujrah 'ala al-Hadanah": He wrote it as a response to a fatwa incident.
30 - "Tahrir al-Nuqul fi Nafaqat al-Furu' wa'l-Usul": He intended by compiling it to explain the guidelines and rules that facilitate the learner's understanding of these precise issues without falling into error and delusion. He completed it in Shawwal of the year 1235.
31 "Raf' al-Intiqad wa Daf' al-I'tirad 'ala Qawlihim: 'al-Ayman Mabniyyah 'ala al-Alfaz la 'ala al-Aghrad'" : He explained in it what they mean by building oaths on words.

Introduction to the Investigation
23
Biography of the Author
clarifying that principle with what pertains to oaths. He finished writing it in Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1238.
-32 "Raf' al-Ishtibah 'an 'Ibarat al-Ashbah": It is a commentary on a phrase in "al-Ashbah wa'l-Naza'ir" by Ibn Nujaym regarding the infallibility of prophets, and an analysis of that issue. He compiled it in compliance with the order of his teacher al-'Aqqad when he referred the answer to him. He completed it in Ramadan of the year 1218.
33 - "Tanbih al-Wulat wa'l-Hukkam 'ala Ahkam Shatim Khayr al-Anam, aw Ahad Ashabihi al-A'lam 'alayhi wa 'alayhim al-Salat wa'l-Salam": It is a treatise he wrote in response to Shaykh 'Abd al-Sattar al-Atasi, the mufti of Homs at the time, when he saw his words in "Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya" regarding the ruling on one who insults the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him and his family). Then he added to it the rulings on one who insults one of his noble Companions. He finished writing it in Jumada al-Ula of the year 1237 AH. So this treatise became an analysis of that issue and a verification of its rulings.
34 - "al-Aqwal al-Wadiha al-Jaliyya": It is an explanation and clarification of an issue mentioned by al-Subki in "al-Ashbah" regarding the annulment of division. He included most of this treatise in his gloss on "al-Ashbah" 150-176. Then he attributed it to "Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya".
35 - "al-'Uqud al-Durriyya fi Qawl al-Waqif: 'ala al-Faridah al-Shar'iyya'": A response to a question about the meaning of "al-Faridah al-Shar'iyya" in the division of a quarter of a waqf on its beneficiaries according to the Sharia allotment. It is a summary with verification of the treatise "al-Risalah al-Mardiyya" by the scholar Ibn al-Minqar. He finished its composition around the year 1230.
36 - "Ghayat al-Matlab fi Ishtirat al-Waqif 'Awd al-Nasib ila Ahl al-Darajah al-Aqrab fa'l-Aqrab": A response to a question sent to him from Tripoli, Syria, along with some fatwas. This treatise became a verification of those fatwas and a scrutiny of that issue.
He completed it in the year 1249 AH.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of the author's works. It continues the author's biography by enumerating his scholarly writings from number 25 to 36. Each entry includes the title, the reason for writing, and often the completion date. The works cover a variety of fiqh and usul topics, including rulings on bequests for Quranic recitations, lunar crescent sighting, divorce conditional on months, custody, maintenance, oaths, and waqf. The author demonstrates his expertise in Hanafi jurisprudence by addressing contemporary issues and providing detailed legal analyses. The list serves as a testament to his prolific scholarship and his role as a mufti and teacher.

Key Terms
فتوى (fatwā): A legal opinion issued by a mufti based on Islamic sources.
مفتي (muftī): A jurist qualified to issue fatwas.
رسالة (risālah): A treatise on a specific legal issue.

List of Works by the Hanafi Jurist
Biographical listing of works with descriptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the works of a Hanafi jurist by genre (fatwa, commentary, usul) and explain their role in the mufti's training.

Core Idea
A mufti's works reflect the full spectrum of Hanafi legal practice — from fatwa compilation to usul clarification.

This passage presents a catalogue of treatises written by the author of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. Far from a mere list, it reveals the scholarly trajectory of a mufti engaged in responding to real fatwa queries, refining legal methodology, and critically engaging with earlier works. By parsing this list, you will gain insight into the practical and theoretical dimensions of Hanafi ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main genres
Scan the list and categorize each work as a fatwa response, a commentary/shurah, a usul method treatise, or a critical review. Note the distinct features of each genre.
Look for keywords like 'جواب', 'شرح', 'تحقيق', 'تعقب'.
2
Note the authorities referenced
Identify the scholars or works cited in each description (e.g., Ibn Nujaym, al-Subki, al-Shurunbulali). Understanding the chain of authority is crucial for evaluating the jurist's intellectual lineage.
These references show the author's engagement with prior Hanafi authorities.
3
Understand the occasion for each treatise
Many works are responses to specific fatwa queries from other muftis or judges. Determine the motivating factor: a dispute, a public misconception, or a request for clarification.
The occasion often explains the work's structure and argumentative focus.
4
Relate each work to the discipline of ifta
Consider how each treatise contributes to the art of fatwa: some provide precedents, others refine methodology, and some correct errors. This helps you appreciate the comprehensive nature of a mufti's scholarship.
For example, 'Nashr al-Urf' directly addresses the role of custom in legal reasoning.

He included most of this treatise in his commentary on 'al-Ashbah' [pages] 150-176. Then he attributed it to 'Tanqih al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya'.

Biography of the author
37- The Clear Explanation that the Endowment of Two Persons for Themselves is One Endowment, Not Two: It is a response to a fatwa that came to him from Tripoli, refuting a fatwa he had issued about a year before this treatise. He mentioned in it the question and the answer of the respondent, then refuted that and clarified the error from the truth. He completed it in Ramadan 1351, one year [after?].
38- Warning the Sleepers concerning the Issues of Currency: He compiled in it the statements of the imams on the rise, fall, circulation, and cessation of currency, and other matters. He did not mention the reason for its composition. He finished it around the year 1230.
39- Perfecting the 'Tahrir' in Invalidating Cases by Rescission due to Gross Disparity without Deception: It is a clarification of a question and answer from Sidon, in which a disturbance occurred between him and the mufti there. So he wrote this treatise as a response to the mufti of Sidon and his deputy, his brother, regarding their attack on the aforesaid scholar. He completed that in Jumada al-Akhira of the year 1248.
40- Warning the Intelligent of the Invalidity of the Ruling on Dismissing the Claim after a General Acquittal: He wrote it in response to an incident where he had clarified the truth, but the religious judge rejected his opinion. So this treatise was a response to that judge, supported with evidences and verified with proofs. It was completed in the year 1251.
41- Informing the Luminaries of the Rulings of General Acknowledgment: It is a verification and elucidation of the issue of general acknowledgment. He verified in it the treatise 'Tanqih al-Ahkam' by al-Shurunbulali, displayed its problematic points, followed up its ambiguities, and added to it numerous quotations. He completed it in the year 1237.
42- Spreading the Custom concerning Building Some Rulings on Custom: It is a critique of his commentary on the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', and a correction of his explanation of the verse which says: 'Custom in the Sharia has consideration, therefore upon it the ruling may be based.' He finished its writing in Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1243 AH.
43- Precision of Expression concerning Who is More Entitled to Rent: It is a clarification of what was prevalent among the commoners at that time, that the first renter is more entitled to rent than anyone else. And it addresses the remaining...
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of the scholarly works of a Hanafi jurist, likely the author of the book itself. It provides the titles and brief descriptions of numerous treatises he wrote, covering a wide range of fiqh topics such as oaths, blasphemy, waqf, currency, rental disputes, and legal procedure. Many of these works are responses to specific questions (fatawa) from other scholars or judges, indicating the author's active role in the legal community. The list also includes works on usul al-fiqh and the methodology of fatwa, such as 'Nashr al-Urf' which deals with the role of custom in Islamic law. This biographical overview demonstrates the depth and breadth of the author's contributions to the Hanafi school. The passage is cut off at the end, listing the beginning of the 43rd work.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): The methodology or 'manual' of the mufti, a genre of Hanafi literature that sets out the principles and procedures for issuing fatawa.
التنقيح (Tanqih): A 'refinement' or 'critical review' of a text, often used in titles of legal works that clarify or correct previous compilations.
العرف (al-Urf): Customary practice recognized as a legal source in the Hanafi school, particularly when it does not contradict explicit texts.

Author's Works (37-50) – A Mufti's Scholarly Output
List of the author's works with descriptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the author's works from 37 to 50 and describe the main subject or occasion of each work.

Core Idea
The author's works show a mufti actively engaged with real-world issues through fatwas and legal clarifications.

This lesson surveys the later works of our author, from number 37 to 50. These treatises cover a wide range of topics: fatwa responses, currency rulings, inheritance, grammar, and spiritual matters. Studying this list helps you appreciate the depth and practical relevance of the Hanafi tradition, and provides a resource for citing authoritative works in fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list and note the variety of topics
Quickly read through each entry, observing the subjects: fatwa corrections, currency, fraud, custom (urf), inheritance, supplications, and more. This gives an overview of the author's expertise.
2
For each work, identify the subject and occasion
Read the description of each work and note what prompted its writing—often a fatwa request or a dispute. For example, work 37 responds to a fatwa from Tripoli, while work 42 corrects his own commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
3
Memorize the titles in order
Use the numbering to commit the Arabic titles to memory. Group them: 37-40 are fatwa-related, 41-44 are legal clarifications, 45-46 deal with arithmetic and inheritance, 47-48 are spiritual, and 49-50 cover grammar and Hajj supplications.
4
Note the dates to see the timeline
The completion dates range from 1224 to 1351 AH. This reveals a long career spanning over a century. Observe which works were written in response to immediate events and which are systematic treatises.

۳۷- غاية البيان في أن وقف الاثنين على أنفسهما وقف لا وقفان : وهو جواب عن فتوى جاءته من طرابلس تُردّ فتوى كان قد أصدرها قبل هذه الرسالة بنحو عام، فذكر فيها السؤال وجواب المجيب، ثم ردّ ذلك وبين الخطأ فيه من الصواب. وأتمها في رمضان ۱۳۵۱ بعام واحد .
۳۸- تنبيه الرقود على مسائل النقود جمع فيها أقوال الأئمة في غلاء النقود، وكسادها، ورواجها، وانقطاعها، وغير ذلك . ولم يبين الحامل على تصنيفها . فرغ منها حدود سنة ١٢٣٠ .
٣٩- تحبير التحرير فى إبطال القضايا بالفسخ بالغبن الفاحش بلا تغرير : وهى تحرير لسؤال وجواب من صيدا " ، وقع فيه اضطراب بينه وبين المفتى فيها ، فحرر هذه الرسالة جواباً لمفتى صيدا ونائبها أخيه عن تهجمها على العلامة المترجم . وقد فرغ من ذلك في جمادى الآخرة من سنة ١٢٤٨ .
٤٠ - تنبيه ذوى الأفهام على بطلان الحكم بنقض الدعوى بعد الإبراء العام ألفها جوابًا على حادثة كان قد بين الصواب فيها، فردّ عليه الحاكم الشرعى، فكان هذه الرسالة جواباً لذلك الحاكم مؤبدة بالأدلة موثقة بالبراهين . وتمت سنة ١٢٥١ .
٤١ - إعلام الأعلام بأحكام الإقرار العام: وهى تحقيق وإيضاح لمسألة الإقرار العام حقق فيها رسالة تنقيح الأحكام للشرنبلالي، وأظهر مشكلاتها، وتعقب مبهماتها، وأضاف إليها نقولا كثيرة أتمها سنة ١٢٣٧ .
٤٢ - نشر العرف فى بناء بعض الأحكام على العرف : وهى تعقب لشرحه على منظومة "عقود رسم المفتى"، واستدراك لشرح بيته الذي يقول : والعرف فى الشرع له اعتبار لذا عليه الحكم قد يدار فرغ من تحريرها في ربيع الثاني من سنة ١٢٤٣هـ.
٤٣ - تحرير العبارة فيمن هو أحق بالإجارة : وهي تجرير لما اشتهر بين العوام آنئذ من أن المستأجر الأول أحق ممن عداه بالإجارة. وتعرض لبـقـيـة أحكام المستأجرين وإيضاح أحوالهم . وتمت في ربيع الثاني سنة ١٢٤٦هـ.
٤٤ - أجوبة محققة عن أسئلة متفرقة : وهى مجموعة من المسائل من بقاع متعددة، ومواضيع متفرقة وتواريخ مختلفة . أجاب عنها كعادته بعبارة واضحة، وحجة بينة، وتحقيق باهر،
٤٥ - مناهل السرور لمبتغى الحساب بالكسور وهي منظومة في الحساب والكسور في سبعة عشر ومائة بيت ويليها - طبعا - منظومة في الزحاف المفرد والمزدوج. وعلل النقص والزيادة الشعرية في ثمانية عشر بيتاً .
٤٦ - الرحيق المختوم شرح قلائد المنظوم: وهو شرح لمنظومة قلائد المنظوم" نظم بها العلامة عبد الرحمن بن إبراهيم الشهير بـ ابن عبد الرزاق " نظم باب الفرائض من ملتقى الأبحر" في ٣٩٢ بيت . فرغ من تسويد الشرح في ذي القعدة سنة ١٢٢٦هـ.
٤٧ - إجابة الغوث ببيان حال النقباء والنجباء والأبدال والأوتاد والغوث وهي رسالة جمعها بسؤال وجه إليه عن أمر القطب والغوث : والأبدال وغير ذلك . ثم استدرك عليها بعض الأمور، وألحقها بها. وقدختمها بتوسله بهم في قصيدة بائية من ستة وعشرين بيتا . وتم الفراغ منها في شوال سنة ١٢٢٤
٤٨ - نسل الحسام الهندى لنصرة مولانا خالد النقشبندي : ألفها ردا على بعض الحاسدين الطاعنين فى العلامة الجليل، ذى الجناحين، المولى خالد النقشبندى مؤيداً ذلك بحال الشيخ وقاله ومريديه . وختمها برؤية رآها أنه صلى على سيدنا عثمان، فأخبره الشيخ أنه من أولاد عثمان، وأنه يموت ويصلّى عليه، فكان كما قال ، ثم عقبها برثاء للمولى خاند رحمه الله تعالى .
٤٩ - الفوائد العجيبة في إعراب الكلمات الغريبة : وهى إعراب لبعض الألفاظ المشتهرة بين العلماء مما فيه إشكال وخفاء .
٥٠ - بغية الناسك في أدعية المناسك : وهو مجموعة من أدعية المناسك،
37- Ghayat al-Bayan concerning that the waqf of two persons upon themselves is one waqf, not two waqfs: It is a response to a fatwa that came to him from Tripoli, refuting a fatwa he had issued about a year before this treatise. He mentioned the question and the answer of the respondent, then refuted that and distinguished error from correctness. He completed it in Ramadan 1351 in one year. 38- Tanbih al-Ruqood on matters of currencies: He compiled in it the statements of the imams regarding the rise, fall, circulation, cessation, and other aspects of currencies. He did not state the motive for its composition. He finished it around the year 1230. 39- Tahrir al-Tahrir on invalidating cases by annulment due to gross fraud without deception: It is a clarification of a question and answer from Sidon, in which there occurred confusion between him and the mufti there. He wrote this treatise as a response to the mufti of Sidon and his deputy, his brother, regarding their attack on the distinguished scholar (the author). He finished that in Jumada al-Akhirah of the year 1248. 40- Tanbih Dhawi al-Afham on the invalidity of a ruling to dismiss a claim after a general acquittal: He authored it as a response to an incident in which he had clarified the correct position, but the shar'i judge rejected it. This treatise was a response to that judge, supported by proofs and substantiated by evidences. It was completed in the year 1251. 41- I'lam al-A'lam bi Ahkam al-Iqrar al-'Am: It is a verification and clarification of the issue of general acknowledgment (iqrar 'am), in which he verified the treatise Tanqih al-Ahkam of Shurunbulali, elucidated its problematic points, pursued its ambiguities, and added many quotations. He completed it in the year 1237. 42- Nashr al-'Urf fi Bina' Ba'd al-Ahkam 'ala al-'Urf: It is a critique of his own commentary on the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, and a correction to the explanation of its verse that says: 'Custom in Shari'ah has consideration, so upon it rulings may be based.' He finished writing it in Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1243 AH. 43- Tahrir al-'Ibarah fi Man Huwa Ahaqq bi al-Ijarah: It is a clarification of what was famous among the common people at that time that the first lessor has more right than others to the lease. He also addressed the remaining rulings concerning lessees and clarified their conditions. It was completed in Rabi' al-Thani of the year 1246 AH. 44- Ajwibah Muhaqqaqah 'an As'ilah Mutafarriqah: It is a collection of issues from various regions, diverse topics, and different dates. He answered them in his usual manner with clear expression, evident proof, and brilliant verification. 45- Manahil al-Surur li Mubtagha al-Hisab bi al-Kusur: It is a poem on arithmetic and fractions consisting of one hundred and seventeen verses, followed by a poem on single and double metrical alteration, and it explains poetic deficiency and excess in eighteen verses. 46- al-Rahiq al-Makhtum Sharh Qala'id al-Manzum: It is a commentary on the poem 'Qala'id al-Manzum' in which the scholar 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ibrahim, known as Ibn 'Abd al-Razzaq, versified the chapter on inheritance from Multaqa al-Abhar in 392 verses. He finished writing the commentary in Dhu al-Qa'dah of the year 1226 AH. 47- Ijabat al-Ghawth bi Bayan Hal al-Nuqaba' wa al-Nujaba' wa al-Abdal wa al-Awtad wa al-Ghawth: It is a treatise he compiled in response to a question directed to him concerning the matter of the Qutb and Ghawth, and al-Abdal and other matters. Then he corrected some matters and attached them. He concluded it with his supplication through them in a poem of twenty-six verses rhyming in 'ba'. It was completed in Shawwal of the year 1224. 48- Nasl al-Husam al-Hindi li Nusrat Mawlana Khalid al-Naqshbandi: He authored it in refutation of some envious attackers upon the venerable scholar, the two-winged one, Mawlana Khalid al-Naqshbandi, supporting that by the state of the shaykh, his saying, and his disciples. He concluded it with a vision he saw that he prayed over our master 'Uthman, and the shaykh informed him that he (the author) was from the descendants of 'Uthman, and that he would die and (the shaykh) would pray over him, and it happened as he said. Then he appended a eulogy for Mawlana Khalid, may Allah have mercy on him. 49- al-Fawa'id al-'Ajibah fi I'rab al-Kalimat al-Gharibah: It is an i'rab of some words that are famous among scholars but which involve difficulty and obscurity. 50- Bughyat al-Nasik fi Ad'iyat al-Manasik: It is a collection of supplications for the rituals (of Hajj).
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list of the author's works, from number 37 to 50. Each entry provides the title and a brief description of the work's purpose, occasion, and completion date. These works cover a wide range of topics including fatwa responses, legal maxims (qawaid), inheritance, grammar, and spiritual matters. The author is meticulous in documenting each work's context, often mentioning the fatwa or incident that prompted its writing. This demonstrates his active role as a mufti responding to real-world issues. The dates given span from 1224 to 1351 AH, indicating a long scholarly career. Note the importance of 'urf (custom) in work 42, which directly relates to the book's theme of 'Rasm al-Mufti'. Work 44 shows his practice of collecting scattered fatwas. The list confirms his expertise in both fiqh and ancillary sciences like arithmetic and poetry.

The Author's Scholarly Works and Their Significance
Listing the author's works and biographical details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the author’s major works and explain how they demonstrate his expertise in Hanafi fiqh and usul al-iftaa.

Core Idea
The author's vast output establishes his authority as a Hanafi mufti.

This passage from the introduction lists the author’s works, spanning fiqh rulings, poetry, usul al-fiqh glosses, and spiritual treatises. Understanding this breadth is essential because a mufti’s scholarly output underpins his reliability in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify Subject Categories
Scan the list and group the works by topic: fiqh (e.g., rulings on tenants), usul al-fiqh (e.g., gloss on al-Manar), hadith (e.g., chain register), poetry, and spiritual matters.
Note works numbered 44–54 plus earlier mentions.
2
Note Fiqh and Usul Works
Focus on works directly relevant to Hanafi fatwa methodology. For example, 'Nasamat al-Ashar' is a gloss on al-Manar in usul al-fiqh, and 'Aqood al-La'ali' deals with hadith chains.
Also note the commentary on inheritance (al-Rahiq al-Makhtum).
3
Recognize Poetic and Spiritual Works
The author wrote poems praising the Prophet and treatises on spiritual ranks. These show his piety and broader scholarship, which complement his legal authority.
Consider how these works might influence his fatwa methodology (e.g., istihsan basen on maqasid).
4
Assess the Relevance to Iftaa
Reflect on how each work contributes to the mufti's toolkit. For instance, the gloss on al-Manar provides usul principles, while the answers to questions demonstrate practical application of ijtihad.
This breadth reinforces the mufti's ability to handle diverse cases.

Among them is a poem he sent to be recited before the Prophet's chamber with the Hajj caravan in the year 1220. It is in praise of the Master of Existence in seventy-one verses rhyming in 'nun'. Its opening: 'Labbayka ya qamariyyat al-aghsān...' He also has a poem rhyming in 'mim' in fifty-seven verses seeking intercession through our master the Messenger of God, may God bless him and his family and grant them peace, in which he mentioned nearly thirty of his miracles, may peace be upon him. Its opening: 'Ashku ila Allah ma alqahu min nasab...' And among his verses: 'And miracles followed before his mission; every blind person would see them with his own eyes.'

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author (ترجمة المصنف) from the introduction of the book. It lists many of the author's works, covering various fields: fiqh (e.g., rulings on tenants), answers to questions, poetry on arithmetic, commentary on inheritance, treatises on spiritual ranks (nuqaba', nujaba', abdal, awtad, ghawth), refutations of critics, linguistic works, prayer collections, usul al-fiqh glosses, hadith chains, and more. The author also composed many poems, including a poem recited before the Prophet's chamber and a poem listing miracles of the Prophet. This overview establishes the author's scholarly authority and breadth of knowledge, which is relevant for understanding the weight of his work in usul al-iftaa.

Biography of the Author: Context for 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
Biographical overview of the author's works, poetry, and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's major works and place 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti within his scholarly output and Hanafi ifta tradition.

Core Idea
The author's short life produced essential works on fatwa methodology, including the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.

This biographical passage introduces you to the author of the text you are studying. Understanding his scholarly background and the range of his works helps contextualize why his poem on the rules of issuing fatwas was necessary and how it fits into the Hanafi tradition. We will parse the details of his life and writings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's scholarly profile
Note that the author was a Hanafi scholar who studied under teachers like Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad and Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. He was buried near al-Haskafi, indicating his connection to the Hanafi school.
The author's name is not explicitly given in this excerpt but is known from the work title.
2
List the author's works
Go through the list: Fath al-Qadir, Manasik al-Imadi, Lubab al-Manasik, Nasamat al-Ashar (gloss on al-Manar), 'Uqud al-La'ali (hadith register), Maqamat (praising teacher), Nuzhat al-Nawazir (gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir), and his poems including 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
These works span fiqh, usul, hadith, and poetry.
3
Examine the poetic output
The author wrote many poems, including a long poem praising the Prophet (71 verses) and a poem seeking intercession (57 verses). His didactic poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti is the focus of this study.
The passage includes excerpts from his poetry.
4
Analyze the details of his death
He died on Wednesday, 21 Rabi' al-Thani 1252 AH at age 54. He was buried near al-Haskafi and al-Jinini in Damascus. His teacher wept over him, saying he had saved him for after his own white hair.
This shows the high regard in which he was held.
5
Reflect on the significance of his short life
Despite only 54 years, his scholarly output was extensive. This underscores the value of focused effort and the Barakah of time in Islamic scholarship.
This relates to the Hanafi emphasis on productive learning.

فالضب كلمه والجذع حنّ له والبدر شق له من باهر الحكم والشمس قد وقفت من بعد ما غربت والسحب قد وكفت لما دعا بفم
ومنها قوله :
فليس بعد الذي في النجم من عظم وبعد ما في الضحى مع نون والقلم فيا رسولا به الرحمن أنقذنا وقد حمانا برکن غیر مندم يا من إذا لاذ مأسور الذنوب به غدا غداً آمنا كالصيد بالحرم وله منظومة عقود رسم المفتى " . وله رثاء للعلامة الكزبري يقول فيها
مؤرخا :
إمامنا الكزبرى نجم لقد أفلا فليل جلّقه ما زال مندلا
وفاته :
لم يكن العلامة المترجم ممن عمر طويلا بما يتناسب مع إنتاجاته العلمية، بل على العكس كانت حياته قصيرة بالنسبة لما ترك، ولكن عمر حياة سعيدة مرضى الوالدين بطاعة الله عزّ وجلّ، بعلم وفير ، وعمل غزير، إلى أن اشتاقت نفسه للقاء ربه، فلبّت راضية مرضية فى يوم الأربعاء الحادي والعشرين من ربيع الثاني سنة اثنتين وخمسين ومائتين وألف للهجرة النبوية . وصلى عليه شيخه الشيخ سعيد الـحـلـبـي. وبـكـي عـلـيـه بـرثاءه ، فقال -وقد أمسك لحيته - : "كنت أدخرك لما بعد هذا الشيب" في مسجد السنانية . ودفن بوصية منه - قرب الشيخ علاء الدين الحصکفی صاحب الدر"، وبجوار العلامة المحدث صالح الجينيني في باب الصغير بمقبرة دمشق. وكان له من العمر أربعة وخمسون عاماً فقط . رحمه الله تعالى رحمة واسعة، وأسكنه فسيح جناته وأعلى منازله .

Introduction to the Investigation - 26 - Biography of the Author. He collected from 'Fath al-Qadir' and 'Manasik al-Imadi' and 'Lubab al-Manasik'... 51 - Nasamat al-Ashar 'ala Ifadat al-Anwar: commentary on the book al-Manar in Usul al-Fiqh; it is the minor gloss on the commentary of al-Haskafi on 'al-Manar' by al-Nasafi. It was mentioned under number 9. 52 - 'Uqud al-La'ali fi al-Asanid al-'Awali: his register of the chains of his teachers, with biographies and permissions from them. 53 - Maqamat in praise of his teacher, Shaykh Shakir al-'Aqqad, may Allah have mercy on him. 54 - Nuzhat al-Nawazir 'ala al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir: his gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym, compiled by his student Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Baytar from the margin of his copy, recently printed in Damascus. The author had many poems, didactic verses, elegies, congratulations, praises, regulations, riddles, and others. Among them is a poem he sent to be recited before the Prophet's chamber accompanying the pilgrimage caravan in the year 1220. It praises the Master of Existence in seventy-one verses rhyming in 'nun'. Its opening: 'Labayk, O moon-like one of the branches, you have rent my heart with melodies...' He also has a poem rhyming in 'mim' in fifty-seven verses seeking intercession through our master the Messenger of Allah, mentioning nearly thirty of his miracles. Its opening: 'I complain to Allah of the fatigue I suffer, seeking intercession through the intercessor of all creation.' Among his lines: 'And miracles followed before his mission; he would see with his eye every blind person; the lizard spoke to him, the trunk yearned for him, the moon was split for him from the dazzling judgments; the sun stopped after it had set, the clouds poured when he called with his mouth.' And among his lines: 'There is nothing after what is in the Star of greatness, and what is in al-Duha with the Nun and the Pen. O Messenger through whom the Merciful saved us, and protected us with a pillar that is not demolished. O you whom if a captive of sins seeks refuge, he becomes tomorrow secure like the game in the sanctuary.' He has the didactic poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. He has an elegy for the scholar al-Kuzbari, in which he says, dating: 'Our imam al-Kuzbari, a star, has set, so a night has darkened him, still pouring.' His death: The author was not one who lived long in proportion to his scholarly output; on the contrary, his life was short relative to what he left behind. But he lived a happy life, pleasing his parents by obedience to Allah, with abundant knowledge and extensive work, until his soul yearned to meet his Lord, and it responded content and pleasing on Wednesday, the twenty-first of Rabi' al-Thani, 1252 AH. His teacher Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi led his funeral prayer and wept over him with an elegy, and said, holding his beard: 'I was saving you for after this white hair.' He was buried in the al-Sananiya mosque, according to his will, near Shaykh 'Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi, author of al-Durr, and next to the scholar al-Muhaddith Salih al-Jinini in Bab al-Saghir cemetery of Damascus. He was only fifty-four years old. May Allah have abundant mercy on him, admit him to His spacious gardens, and raise his ranks.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. It lists several of his works, indicating his scholarly activity in fiqh, usul al-fiqh, hadith, and poetry. The mention of his poem on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' directly links to the present book. The biography emphasizes his early death at 54 despite a prolific output, and notes his burial near prominent Hanafi scholars like al-Haskafi (author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar). The passage also includes poetic excerpts, praising the Prophet and elegizing another scholar. For students, this shows the author's scholarly lineage and the context of his work on the rules of issuing fatwas.

Key Terms
عقود رسم المفتى ('Uqud Rasm al-Mufti): A didactic poem (manzuma) by the author on the rules and methodology of issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school.
الأشباه والنظائر (al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir): A major Hanafi work on legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyya) by Ibn Nujaym. The author wrote a gloss on it.
المنار في أصول الفقه (al-Manar fi Usul al-Fiqh): A well-known Hanafi usul al-fiqh text by al-Nasafi. The author wrote a gloss on al-Haskafi's commentary.

Biography of the Author of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
Biographical account of the author's life and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Uqud Rasm al-Mufti and describe key biographical details, including his death date and scholarly context.

Core Idea
A short life can yield lasting scholarly contributions.

Before studying a text, it is essential to know its author — his life, his teachers, and the context in which he wrote. This biographical sketch introduces you to the scholar behind the poetic work Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, a foundational text in Hanafi fatwa methodology. His early death at 54 reminds us that quality, not quantity, defines scholarly legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his main work
Note that the passage does not name the author explicitly, but refers to him as 'al-muṣannif' (the author). His main work is the versified text 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' on the rules of fatwa issuance.
The author is likely a later Hanafi scholar, possibly Ibn Abidin or a commentator on his work.
2
Analyze the poetic tributes
The passage begins with poetic lines describing miracles (e.g., the trunk yearning, the moon splitting). These are allusions to the Prophet's miracles, honoring the author's connection to him. Also note the elegy for al-Kuzbari.
These lines establish the author's piety and his reverence for the Prophet and his teachers.
3
Examine the death details
The author died on Wednesday, 21 Rabi' al-Thani 1252 AH (1836 CE) at age 54. His teacher led the funeral prayer, and he was buried near prominent scholars in Damascus.
The date is precisely given; you should memorize it for context.
4
Understand his scholarly position
Despite a short life, he produced significant work. The fact that he is buried near 'Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi (author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar) indicates his high rank in Hanafi scholarship.
This situates him in the Damascene Hanafi tradition.
5
Connect to iftaa methodology
Uqud Rasm al-Mufti is a poetic text on fatwa procedure. Knowing the author's background helps you appreciate the work's reliability and the tradition it represents.
You will encounter references to this work in later lessons on fatwa methodology.

Introduction to the Verification: Biography of the Author. The lizard spoke to him, the trunk yearned for him, the moon split for him from the dazzling wonders, and the sun stopped after it had set, and the clouds poured when he called with his mouth. Among his sayings: 'Nothing after what is in the Star and what is in the Forenoon and the Nun and the Pen, O Messenger through whom the Merciful saved us, and He protected us with an unbreakable pillar. O he who, when a captive of sins seeks refuge with him, becomes in the morning safe like game in the sanctuary.' And he has the versification 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. And he has an elegy for al-Allama al-Kuzbari in which he says, dating: 'Our Imam al-Kuzbari, a star has set, so may a night swathe him, which continues to be like a shroud.' His death: The translated scholar was not among those who lived long commensurate with his scholarly output; rather, his life was short relative to what he left. But he lived a happy life, pleasing his parents through obedience to Allah Almighty, with abundant knowledge and plentiful action, until his soul longed to meet his Lord, and it responded contentedly and pleasingly on Wednesday, the twenty-first of Rabi' al-Thani, the year 1252 AH. His teacher, Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi, prayed over him. He wept over him with his elegy, and said—holding his beard—'I was saving you for after this grey hair' in the Sananiyya Mosque. He was buried by his will—near Shaykh 'Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi, author of al-Durr, and next to the great hadith scholar Salih al-Jinini in Bab al-Saghir in the cemetery of Damascus. He was only fifty-four years old. May Allah have vast mercy on him, lodge him in His spacious gardens, and elevate his ranks.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a biography of the author of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', likely the commentator Ibn 'Abidin or a similar figure, though the name is not explicitly given here. It begins with poetic lines praising the author's miraculous signs, then mentions his poetic work 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', an elegy for al-Kuzbari, and details of his death. The author died at a relatively young age (54) on Wednesday, 21 Rabi' al-Thani 1252 AH (1836 CE). His teacher Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi led the funeral prayer, and he was buried near the grave of Shaykh 'Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi (the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar) in the Bab al-Saghir cemetery in Damascus. This biography provides essential context for understanding the work, highlighting the author's scholarly stature and the heritage of Hanafi fiqh in Damascus.

Key Terms
المصنف (al-muṣannif): The author of the work being commented on, i.e., the author of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' (likely Muhammad Amin ibn 'Abidin or the like).
عقود رسم المفتى (ʿuqūd rasm al-muftī): The title of the author's poetic work on the rules and methodology for issuing fatwas.
العلامة الكزبري (al-ʿallāma al-kuzbarī): A scholar for whom the author wrote an elegy; presumably a contemporary or teacher.

The Compilation and Significance of al-Jami' al-Saghir
Narrating the background and importance of al-Jami' al-Saghir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the reason for compiling al-Jami' al-Saghir, the number of mas'alahs it contains, and explain its authoritative status in the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is the most relied-upon Hanafi text, compiled by Muhammad at Abu Yusuf's request.

Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a foundational text of the Hanafi school, but how did it come to be? This passage gives us the biographical context: why it was compiled, how many mas'alahs it covers, and why it became a benchmark for qadi's. Understanding this history helps you appreciate the text's authority in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compiler and reason for compilation
Confirm that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani compiled it at the request of Abu Yusuf, who wanted a book to narrate from Abu Hanifa.
2
Count the mas'alahs and note the book's status
The book contains 1532 mas'alahs as per al-Bazdawi. It is described as 'blessed' and Abu Yusuf never parted from it.
The number is sometimes cited as 1532, but variations exist.
3
Understand the incident of the six mas'alahs
When presented, Abu Yusuf praised Muhammad's memory but claimed he misremembered six mas'alahs. Muhammad asserted he memorized them correctly and Abu Yusuf forgot.
This shows the high level of accuracy expected and Muhammad's authority.
4
Recognize the book's use as a test for qadis
Ali al-Razi said whoever understands this book is the most understanding among Hanafis. Qadi candidates were examined on it before appointment.
The book became a standard for competence.

And he said: 'Indeed al-Jami' al-Saghir was authored by Muhammad after al-Asl, so what is in it is relied upon.' The reason for its compilation: Abu Yusuf asked him to compile a book that he could narrate from him from Abu Hanifa, so he compiled it for him, then presented it to him and it pleased him. It is a blessed book containing 1532 mas'alahs, as al-Bazdawi said. Some mentioned: Abu Yusuf, despite his great rank, never parted from it (the book) in travel or at home. Ali al-Razi used to say: 'Whoever understands this book is the most understanding of our companions.' And they would not appoint anyone to the judiciary until they examined him with it. In Ghayat al-Bayan from Fakhr al-Islam: When al-Jami' al-Saghir was presented to Abu Yusuf, he approved it and said: 'Abu Abdullah (Muhammad) memorized' (except for some mas'alahs he erred in narrating from him). Muhammad said: 'I memorized them, but he forgot.' They are six mas'alahs (mentioned in al-Bahr in the chapter of Witr and Nawafil).
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage provides the biographical background of al-Jami' al-Saghir, a key text of the Hanafi madhhab. The author explains that Imam Muhammad compiled it at the request of Abu Yusuf, who wanted a concise work to narrate from Abu Hanifa. The book's significance is highlighted by its number of mas'alahs (1532), the fact that Abu Yusuf carried it everywhere, and that it was used as a test for qadi candidates. The passage also recounts a famous incident where Muhammad corrected Abu Yusuf's recollection of six mas'alahs, demonstrating Muhammad's superior memory and authority. This book is considered so fundamental that understanding it is a sign of deep fiqh knowledge. The footnotes add further details about the number of mas'alahs where there is ikhtilaf and the identity of the narrator of the story.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): The 'Small Compilation' by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, a foundational Hanafi work containing 1532 mas'alahs.
أبو يوسف (Abu Yusuf): The chief disciple of Abu Hanifa and later chief qadi; he requested the compilation of al-Jami' al-Saghir.
المسائل الست (al-masa'il al-sitt): The six mas'alahs that Muhammad claimed Abu Yusuf misremembered; they are detailed in other works.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is the most relied-upon Hanafi concise text, and its compilation history shows the meticulous verification of rulings by the early masters.

The Composition of Al-Jami' al-Saghir and the Six Corrected Narrations
Front-matter: composition and textual corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the historical context of Al-Jami' al-Saghir and explain the significance of the six masail corrections in Hanafi textual criticism.

Core Idea
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is the relied-upon Hanafi text, but six masail were corrected by Abu Yusuf.

This lesson explores why Al-Jami' al-Saghir was composed and examines six specific cases where Abu Yusuf corrected Muhammad's transmission from Abu Hanifa. Understanding these corrections is essential for evaluating narrations in the Hanafi school, ensuring that the mufti relies on the most authentic version of the school's doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Historical context of Al-Jami' al-Saghir
Identify the reason for its compilation: Abu Yusuf requested a book from Muhammad al-Shaybani that he could narrate from him from Abu Hanifa.
2
Authority and content of the book
Note that the book contains 1532 masail, that Abu Yusuf highly valued it, and that it was used as a test for judges. Understand that it is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) text.
3
List the six masail and their corrections
Read through each of the six masail where Abu Yusuf corrected Muhammad's transmission. For each, identify the original ruling and Abu Yusuf's correction.
These masail cover sajdah, mustahadah, purchase from a usurper, marriage of a pregnant woman, blood money, and slavery.
4
Understand the methodology of correction
Analyze why Abu Yusuf made these corrections: he claimed Muhammad had misremembered the rulings. This highlights the importance of verifying narrations and the rigorous standards of the early Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلب في سبب تأليف "الجامع الصغير"
وقال: "إن الجامع الصغير صنّفه محمد بعد "الأصل"، فما فيه هو المعول عليه". اهـ. وسبب تأليفه: أنه طلب منه أبو يوسف أن يجمع له كتاباً يرويه عنه عن أبي حنيفة، فجمعه له، ثم عرضه عليه فأعجبه. وهو كتاب مبارك) يشتمل على ألف وخمسمائة واثنتين وثلاثين مسألة، كما قال البزدوي. وذكر بعضهم): أن أبا يوسف مع جلالة قدره لا يفارقه في سفر ولا حضر. وكان على الرازي يقول: "من فهم هذا الكتاب فهو أفهم أصحابنا". وكانوا لا يقلّدون أحدا القضاء حتى يمتسحنه به.
(1) قوله: هو كتاب مبارك" قال الچلپی إنه ذكر الاختلاف فيه في مائة وسبعين مسألة، ولم يذكر القياس إلا في مسألتين". (مظ)
(2) قوله: ذكر بعضهم هو على بن موسى القمى كما يستفاد من "الكشف". (مظ)
(3) قوله: "وقال: حفظ أبو عبد الله" كذا في النسخة المصرية التي عندي وفي العبارة سقط؛ لأن المذكور في البحر" هكذا: "قال: حفظ أبو عبد الله، إلا مسائل خطاه في روايتها عنه، فلما بلغ ذلك محمداً، قال: أنا حفظتها... إلخ". (مظ)
(4) قوله: وهى ست مسائل" وفى "الكشف": أنها ثلاث مسائل، لكن الظاهر أنها ست، كما ذكرها العلامة السراج الهندى في "شرح المغني"، فقال: الأولى: شخص قرأ في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين يقضى أربعًا، قال أبو يوسف: "وإنما رويت لك أنه يلزمه قضاء ركعتين".
والثانية: مستحاضة توضأت بعد طلوع الشمس تصلى حتى يخرج وقت الظهر، وقال أبو يوسف: "وإنما رويت لك حتى يدخل وقت الظهر". والثالثة: المشترى من الغاصب إذا أعتق، ثم أجاز المالك البيع نفذ العتق، قال: "إنما رويت لك أنه لا ينفذ".
الرابعة: المهاجرة لا عدة عليها، ويجوز نكاحها إلا أن تكون حبلى، فحينئذ لا يجوز نكاحها. قال أبو يوسف: "إنما رويت لك أنه يجوز نكاحها، ولكن لا يقربها زوجها حتى تضع الحمل".
الخامسة: عبد بين اثنين قتل مولى لهما، فعفا أحدهما، بطل الدم كله عند أبى حنيفة، وقالا: يدفع ربعه إلى شريكه أو يفديه بربع الدية، وقال أبو يوسف: "إنما حكيت لك عن أبي حنيفة، كقولنا. وإنما الاختلاف الأ"، رويته في عبد قتل مولاه عمداً، وله ابنان فعفا أحدهما. إلا أن محمداً ذكر الائتلاف فيهما، وذكر قول نفسه مع أبي يوسف في الأولى.
السادسة: رجل مات وترك ابنا له وعبدا لا غير، فادعى العبد: أن الميت كان أعتقه فى صحته، وادعى رجل على الميت ألف دينار، وقيمة العبد ألف، فقال الابن: صدقتما - يسعى العبد في قيمته وهو حر، ويأخذهما الغريم بدينه وقال أبويوسف: إنما رويت لك ما دام يسعى في قيمته أنه عبد. (مظ)
A request concerning the reason for compiling 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir'. He said: 'Indeed, Muhammad compiled Al-Jami' al-Saghir after Al-Asl. What is in it is relied upon.' End. The reason for its compilation: Abu Yusuf asked him to compile a book for him to narrate from him from Abu Hanifa. So he compiled it for him, then presented it to him, and it pleased him. It is a blessed book containing one thousand five hundred and thirty-two masail, as al-Bazdawi said. Some mentioned that Abu Yusuf, despite his high rank, would not part with it during travel or residence. Ali al-Razi used to say: 'Whoever understands this book is the most understanding of our companions.' They would not appoint anyone to judgeship until they tested him with it.
(1) He said: 'It is a blessed book.' Al-Jalabi said that he mentioned disagreement in it in one hundred and seventy masail, and he did not mention analogy except in two masail. (Maz)
(2) He said: 'Some mentioned' is Ali ibn Musa al-Qumi, as derived from 'Al-Kashf'. (Maz)
(3) He said: 'And he said: Abu Abdullah memorized.' This is in the Egyptian copy I have, but in the phrase there is a drop, because what is mentioned in 'Al-Bahr' is thus: 'He said: Abu Abdullah memorized, except for masail in which he erred in narrating them from him. When that reached Muhammad, he said: I memorized them... etc.' (Maz)
(4) He said: 'And they are six masail.' In 'Al-Kashf' they are three masail, but apparently they are six, as mentioned by the scholar Siraj al-Hindi in 'Sharh al-Mughni'. He said: The first: A person recited in one of the first two rak'ats and one of the last two; he must perform four sajdahs. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you that two sajdahs are obligatory upon him.'
The second: A mustahadah who performed wudu after sunrise and prayed until the time of Zuhr exits. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you until the time of Zuhr enters.' The third: The purchaser from a usurper if he frees, then the owner ratifies the sale, the emancipation is effective. He said: 'I only narrated to you that it is not effective.'
The fourth: A fugitive (who emigrated) has no 'iddah, and it is permissible to marry her unless she is pregnant; then it is not permissible to marry her. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you that it is permissible to marry her, but her husband should not approach her until she delivers.'
The fifth: A slave between two owners killed their master. One of them pardoned: the entire blood money is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He hands over one-fourth to his partner or ransoms it with one-fourth of the blood money. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you from Abu Hanifa a statement like ours. But the disagreement is that I narrated it regarding a slave who killed his master intentionally, and he had two sons; one of them pardoned. But Muhammad mentioned the agreement in both, and mentioned his own statement with Abu Yusuf in the first.'
The sixth: A man died leaving a son and a slave, nothing else. The slave claimed that the deceased had freed him during his health. A man claimed that the deceased owed him one thousand dinars, and the slave's value is one thousand. The son said: 'You both are truthful.' The slave works to pay his value and becomes free, and the creditor takes them for his debt. Abu Yusuf said: 'I only narrated to you that as long as he works to pay his value, he is a slave.' (Maz)
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion about the origin and authority of Al-Jami' al-Saghir. It first states that Muhammad al-Shaybani compiled this work after Al-Asl, and that it is the relied-upon text. The reason for compilation was Abu Yusuf's request for a book he could narrate from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa. The text notes that it contains 1532 masail, and that Abu Yusuf and others highly valued it. The marginal notes add details: the first note mentions that the book contains disagreement in 170 masail and only two cases of qiyas. The second identifies the source of the phrase 'some mentioned.' The third discusses a discrepancy in a narration about Muhammad's memory. The fourth and most extensive part lists six specific masail where Abu Yusuf corrected Muhammad's transmission from Abu Hanifa. Each mas'ala presents a ruling and Abu Yusuf's correction, highlighting the importance of verifying narrations. These masail cover topics like sajdah, menstruation, purchase from a usurper, marriage of a pregnant woman, blood money, and slavery. The passage underscores the meticulousness of the early Hanafi scholars in preserving the school's doctrine.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): A major Hanafi fiqh compilation by al-Shaybani, after Al-Asl, containing 1532 masail.
المسائل الست (Al-Masail al-Sitt): Six specific masail where Abu Yusuf corrected Muhammad's transmission from Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many masail does Al-Jami' al-Saghir contain according to al-Bazdawi?
A) One thousand five hundred and thirty-two
B) One thousand seven hundred
C) One thousand three hundred and two
D) Two thousand

Key Takeaway
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is authoritative, but the six masail show that early Hanafi scholars carefully verified transmissions.

The Authority of Mabsut al-Sarakhsi in Hanafi Fatwa
Praise and biographical account of Mabsut al-Sarakhsi and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authoritative status of Mabsut al-Sarakhsi and explain why it is relied upon for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the supreme reference; no fatwa is given contrary to it.

This lesson examines a passage from Rasm al-Mufti that establishes Mabsut al-Sarakhsi as the most authoritative text for Hanafi fatwa. You will learn why scholars insist on exclusive reliance on this work and how its author's extraordinary circumstances (dictating from memory in prison) further attest to its reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about Mabsut's authority
Read the passage and find the direct quote from al-Tartusi that declares one must not act contrary to Mabsut and must rely only on it.
This is the central statement establishing its rank.
2
Examine the evidence supporting the claim
Note the poems and the commentary that praise Mabsut, comparing it to the ocean and unique pearls.
The praise reinforces the authoritative position.
3
Understand the biographical context of its composition
Learn that Imam Sarakhsi dictated Mabsut from memory while imprisoned, which highlights his mastery and the reliability of the text.
The prison story underscores the text's authenticity.
4
Relate this to the hierarchy of Hanafi texts
Recognize that Mabsut is a commentary on Kafi al-Hakim, which summarizes Zahir al-Riwayah, placing it at the top of the fatwa hierarchy.
This connects biographical fact to usul al-iftaa.

(۲) قوله : " فإنه يجاب " هو مبنى للمفعول من الإجابة، وسائله " نائب مناب فاعله. و "الرغائب جمع رغيبة، وهى الأمر المرغوب والعطاء الكثير . (مظ) (۳۰) قوله : أملى المبسوط " نقل في "الفوائد" عن طبقات على القاري أيضاً مثله، لكن ذكر فيه أنه مات سنة ثمان وثلاثين وأربع مائة ، وقيل : في حدود خمسمائة، وقيل: في حدود تسعين وأربعمائة، كما ذكره المصنف . (٥٠٦/٣)
al-Sarakhsi. End. Kafi al-Hakim. Shaykh Ismail al-Nabulsi said: "Allamah Tartusi said: 'Mabsut al-Sarakhsi - one does not act contrary to it, one does not rely except on it, one does not give fatwa or rely except on it.' End. And al-Tamimi (1) mentioned in his Tabaqat many poems praising it, including one recited by someone: 'You must stick to Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, for it is the ocean and its pearls are unique; do not rely except on it, for its seeker is answered by giving abundant gifts.' Allamah Shaykh Hibat Allah al-Ba'li said in his commentary on al-Ashbah: 'Al-Mabsut by the great Imam Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarakhsi, one of the great imams, the mutakallim, faqih, usuli. He studied under Shams al-A'imma 'Abd al-Aziz al-Halwani and graduated under him, until he became the most insightful of his time. He began authoring and dictated al-Mabsut (3) in about ten volumes while in prison in Uzjand, due to a word (4) in which he was among the sincere. He died in the year 490.' (1) His saying 'al-Tamimi' is with fath of the ta and under the ya between two kasra mems. Al-Sam'ani said: attribution to Tamim, and many companions and later generations are attributed to it. (Mazhar) And what is meant here is Allamah Taqi al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Qadir, author of 'al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya.' (2) His saying 'fa innahu yujab' is passive from ijaba, and 'sa'iluhu' is the substitute subject. 'Ragha'ib' is plural of raghiba, meaning desired thing and abundant gift. (Mazhar) (3) His saying 'amla al-Mabsut' is quoted in al-Fawa'id from Tabaqat 'Ali al-Qari similarly, but it mentions that he died in 438, and it was said around 500, and said around 490 as the author mentioned. (Mazhar) (4) His saying 'bi kalima kana fiha min al-nasihin' - in Bab al-'Idda of Radd al-Muhtar: 'It is reported that when Shams al-A'imma was released from prison, the sultan married his ummahat awlad to his free servants, and the scholars approved, but Shams al-A'imma criticized that under each servant there was a free woman, and this is marrying a slave woman over a free woman. So the sultan said: Free them and renew the contract. The scholars approved, but Shams al-A'imma criticized that they must observe 'idda after emancipation. It is said this was the cause of his imprisonment, and that the qadi incited against him, and when the students did not stay away from him, his books were kept from him, so he dictated al-Mabsut from memory.' (3/506)
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and doctrinal account of the status of Mabsut al-Sarakhsi. It begins by quoting Shaykh Ismail al-Nabulsi relaying from Allamah Tartusi that one must not act contrary to the Mabsut, rely only on it, and issue fatwa solely based on it. This establishes its supreme authority in the Hanafi madhhab as a Zahir al-Riwayah text. The passage then cites al-Tamimi's Tabaqat which includes a poem urging reliance on the Mabsut, comparing its rulings to pearls. Next, a description from Shaykh Hibat Allah al-Ba'li identifies Imam Sarakhsi as a leading scholar in kalam, fiqh, and usul, who studied under Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and later dictated the Mabsut from memory while imprisoned in Uzjand. The imprisonment story, elaborated in the fourth footnote from Radd al-Muhtar, relates to a fatwa regarding the sultan's marriage of ummahat awlad, which led to his incarceration and dictation of the Mabsut from memory. This underscores the book's reliability despite being composed under duress. The footnotes provide lexical and biographical clarifications, such as identifying 'al-Tamimi' as Taqi al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Qadir and explaining the passive construction of 'yujab'.

Key Terms
مبسوط (Mabsut): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Imam Sarakhsi, considered the most authoritative reference for fatwa.
كافي الحاكم (Kafi al-Hakim): A mukhtasar by al-Hakim al-Shahid summarising the works of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, on which the Mabsut is a commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Mabsut al-Sarakhsi considered the most authoritative Hanafi reference?
A) Because it was written in a scholarly circle
B) Because scholars declare that one must not act contrary to it and must rely only on it
C) Because it is the longest work
D) Because it was written by a famous judge

Key Takeaway
Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate reference for Hanafi fatwa, and no mufti should rely on a text that contradicts it.
