Reconciling Conflicting Death Dates in Biographical Sources
Biographical entry with conflicting death dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tarjih (preference) when biographical sources give conflicting dates.

Core Idea
Conflicting reports require us to examine the reliability of each source, not simply pick one.

This biographical entry lists two different death years for Ibrahim ibn Yusuf: 241 AH and 239 AH. The first comes from the main text, the second from Abu al-Layth's al-Nawazil. Such discrepancies are common in early biographies. Learning how to reconcile them teaches a vital skill for muftis: weighing sources by their precision and authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
Note the two death dates: one states 'year 241 AH', the other says 'Jumada al-Ula 239 AH'.
The second report is more precise (month and year).
2
Evaluate the source of each report
The first date comes from the main anonymous biographer; the second is from a known Hanafi faqih, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, in his book al-Nawazil.
Abu al-Layth died in 373 AH, relatively close to Ibrahim's time.
3
Apply the principle of tarjih
Prefer the more specific report (month + year) over the general one. Also consider that Abu al-Layth was a meticulous Hanafi jurist.
The commentator does not resolve which is correct, but the principle gives weight to precision.
4
Consider the possibility of multiple transmissions
Death dates could be transmitted differently due to calendar errors, scribal mistakes, or different regional calendars.
The difference is only two years, which could be a simple confusion.
5
Conclude with a practical approach for the mufti
When a precise date is available from a reliable source, it should be given priority. The mufti should note both possibilities humbly.
In fatwa, precise dates matter for issues like inheritance and determining if narrators met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۱- أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن يوسف : هو إبراهيم بن يوسف بن مـيـمــون قدامة البلخي، كان إماماً كبيراً ، وشيخ ،زمانه لزم أبا يوسف حتى برع ، وروى عن سفيان وغيره. وعن مالك حديثاً واحداً عن نافع عن ابن عمر : كل مسكر خمر وكل مسكر حرام فإنه لما دخل على مالك يسمع منه، وقتيبة بن سعد حاضر فقال لمالك : هذا يرى الإرجاء " ، فأمر أن يقام من المجلس فقام ، ولم يسمع غير هذا الحديث . مات. سنة إحدى وأربعين ومائتين. وفي ميزان الاعتدال إبراهيم بن يوسف البلخى الفقيه روى عن حماد بن زيد. وطبقته، ولزم أبا يوسف حتى برع. وثقه النسائى وقال أبو حاتم : " لا يشتغل به " ، قلت : هذا تحامل لأجل الإرجاء الذي فيه . وقد قال ابن حبان : "ظاهره الإرجاء واعتقاده في الباطن السنة وسنذكر أخاه عصام بن يوسف، وأن ابن حبان ذكرهما في الثقات. وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث في آخر كتابه النوازل وفاة إبراهيم في جمادى الأولى سنة تسع وثلاثين ومائتين، ووفاة أخيه عصام سنة خمس عشرة ومائتين .
11- Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Yusuf: He is Ibrahim ibn Yusuf ibn Maymun Qudama al-Balkhi. He was a great imam, the shaykh of his time. He stuck to Abu Yusuf until he excelled. He narrated from Sufyan and others. From Malik, he narrated a single hadith from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar: 'Every intoxicant is khamr and every intoxicant is haram.' For when he entered upon Malik to hear from him, Qutayba ibn Sa'd was present and said to Malik: 'This one holds irja', so he ordered him to be removed from the gathering, so he left and did not hear except this hadith. He died in the year 241 AH. And in Mizan al-I'tidal: Ibrahim ibn Yusuf al-Balkhi al-Faqih narrated from Hammad ibn Zayd and his class, and he stuck to Abu Yusuf until he excelled. Al-Nasa'i declared him trustworthy, but Abu Hatim said: 'Do not occupy yourself with him.' I say: This is bias due to his alleged irja'. Ibn Hibban said: 'His outward shows irja', but his inner belief is the Sunnah.' We will mention his brother 'Isam ibn Yusuf, and that Ibn Hibban mentioned both among the trustworthy. And the faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned in the end of his book al-Nawazil the death of Ibrahim in Jumada al-Ula 239 AH, and the death of his brother 'Isam in 215 AH.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for the Hanafi scholar Ibrahim ibn Yusuf al-Balkhi, a prominent student of Abu Yusuf. The text recounts an incident where Imam Malik expelled him from a gathering due to allegations of irja' (the belief that faith is separate from actions). Despite this, he is praised by al-Nasa'i as trustworthy, and Ibn Hibban defends him. The entry notes conflicting death dates: 241 AH from one source and 239 AH from Abu al-Layth. His brother 'Isam is also mentioned as a trustworthy scholar.

Key Terms
التاريخ (al-ta'rikh): Date, especially of death; crucial in determining the era and transmission links.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The method of preferring one evidence over another based on strength, specificity, or reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which death date for Ibrahim ibn Yusuf is more specific?
A) 241 AH
B) 239 AH in Jumada al-Ula
C) Both are equally specific
D) Neither is specific

Key Takeaway
When sources conflict, prefer more precise reports from reliable authorities; this is a core tarjih skill for a mufti.

The Life and Legacy of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi
Biographical entry detailing the life and scholarship of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, explain his contribution to Hanafi fiqh through Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar, and identify the famous view regarding his madhhab transition.

Core Idea
Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: a Hanafi imam whose works bridged hadith and fiqh, and whose life exemplified scholarly integrity.

Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi is one of the most revered scholars in the Hanafi tradition. This lesson introduces you to his life, his major works, and the controversy around his madhhab transition. Understanding his biography helps appreciate the depth of Hanafi scholarship and the interconnectedness of fiqh and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Read the opening lines to find his complete name and tribal affiliation. Note the chain of ancestors.
This establishes his pedigree and connection to the Azd tribe.
2
Note his birth and death dates
Extract the years of birth and death as given in the text. Be aware of variant reports.
The text gives 230 AH and 321 AH, with other possibilities mentioned.
3
Understand the nisbah and its correction
Analyze the discussion about his attribution to Taha versus Tuhfutah. Why is this significant?
Al-Suyuti corrects the nisbah, showing attention to accurate genealogical attribution.
4
Examine the madhhab transition
Identify the different views on his madhhab journey. Which is the famous opinion?
The famous view is Shafi'i then Hanafi, though some say Maliki was intermediate.
5
Summarize his scholarly contribution
Reflect on his major work Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar and his reputation as a trustworthy imam and faqih.
This work is a key source for Hanafi usul al-fiqh, reconciling hadith with Hanafi rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۲ - أبو جعفر الطحاوي : قال السمعاني : الطحاوي نسبة إلى "طحا . (بفتح الطاء المهملة والحاء المهملة بأسفل أرض مصر، والمشهور بالنسبة إليها ، أبو جعفر أحمد بن محمد بن سلامة بن سلمة بن عبد المالك بن مسلمة بن سليمان الأزدي الطحاوى، صاحب شرح معاني الآثار. كان إماماً، ثقة، فقيها ، عاقلا لم يخلف مثله ، ولد سنة ٢٣٠هـ وتوفى ليلة الخميس مستهل ذى القعدة سنة ٣٢١هـ . وقيل : إنه ولد سنقه ٢٢هـ " . وقيل : سنة ٢٠٣هـ ، كذا في الفوائد، وذكر في هامشه تحت قوله : نسبة إلى طحا" : "هكذا ذكره غير واحد ، لكن قال السيوطى في لب اللباب في تحرير الأنساب " : هو ليس منها، بل من طحطوطة (قرية بقرب طحا) فكره أن يقال له طحطوطي". فائدة : قال القاري في شرح الشفاء في ترجمته : قال بعضهم : كان أولا شافعيا ثم تقلد مذهب مالك، كذا قاله التلماني . ولعله انتقل من مذهب مالك إلى مذهب أبي حنيفة، كما يشهد به كتبه في الرواية والدراية " . والمشهور خلافه : وهو أنه كان أولا شافعيّاً، ثم تقلد مذهب أبي حنيفة . نادرة : في الطحطاوي على الدر" : "حكى عن الطحاوي أنه كان يملى على ابنته مسائل، يقول في إملاءه : ألسنا قد جامعناكم على كذا ، وكنتم قد جامعتمونا على كذا فتبسمت ابنته يوماً من ذلك، فوقع بصره عليها ، فقال : ما شأنك؟ فتبسمت مرة أخرى، فأحس الطحاوى أنها ذهبت إلى الجماع المعروف بهذا اللفظ، فقال: "أو يفهم من هذا، فاحترق غضبا، وقطع الإملاء ورفع يديه إلى السماء، وقال: "اللهم لا أريد حياة بعد هذا، فمات بعد نحو خمسة أيام" .
12- Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi: Al-Sam'ani said: al-Tahawi is a relative attribution to 'Taha' (with a fatha on the unpointed ta and ha, a locality in lower Egypt). The famous person attributed to it is Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Salamah ibn Salamah ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Maslamah ibn Sulayman al-Azdi al-Tahawi, the author of Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar. He was an imam, trustworthy, a jurist, intelligent, who left no equal. He was born in 230 AH and died on the night of Thursday at the beginning of Dhu al-Qa'dah 321 AH. It is said he was born in [؟] 22 AH? And it is said 203 AH, as in al-Fawa'id. And in its margin under his saying 'attribution to Taha': 'Thus mentioned by more than one, but al-Suyuti in Lub al-Lubab fi Tahrir al-Ansab said: He is not from it, but from Tuhfutah (a village near Taha), and he disliked being called Tuhfuti.' Benefit: al-Qari said in Sharh al-Shifa in his biography: Some said he was first a Shafi'i then followed the Maliki school, as stated by al-Talamani. Perhaps he transferred from the Maliki school to the Hanafi school, as evidenced by his writings in riwayah and dirayah. The famous contrary view is that he was first a Shafi'i then followed the Hanafi school. Anecdote: In al-Tuhfawi 'ala al-Durr: It is narrated that al-Tahawi was dictating questions to his daughter, saying in his dictation: 'Have we not had jima' with you on such and such, and you had jima' with us on such and such.' So his daughter smiled one day at that, and his eye fell on her. He said: 'What is the matter with you?' She smiled again. Al-Tahawi realized she had understood the common meaning of jima' as intercourse. He said: 'Can this be understood from this?' He burned with anger, stopped dictation, raised his hands to the sky, and said: 'O Allah, I do not want life after this.' He died after about five days.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, one of the greatest Hanafi scholars, famous for his works like Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar and al-'Aqida al-Tahawiyya. The entry discusses his nisbah (attribution) to Taha, with a marginal note correcting it to Tuhfutah. It then discusses his madhhab transition: some say he was Shafi'i then Maliki, then Hanafi; the famous view is Shafi'i then Hanafi. The anecdote at the end illustrates his extreme modesty and sensitivity to ambiguous language, which led to his death after an unintended misunderstanding with his daughter.

Key Terms
الطحاوي (al-Tahawi): A Hanafi scholar, author of Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar and al-'Aqida al-Tahawiyya.
شرح معاني الآثار (Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar): One of al-Tahawi's major works, explaining the meanings of hadiths related to legal rulings.
النسبة (al-nisbah): A relative attribution indicating a person's place of origin or tribe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what was the famous view regarding al-Tahawi's madhhab transition?
A) He was first Hanafi then Shafi'i
B) He was first Shafi'i then Hanafi
C) He was first Maliki then Hanafi
D) He remained Shafi'i his whole life

Key Takeaway
Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi was a towering Hanafi scholar whose works remain central to Hanafi fiqh and hadith methodology.

A Lesson in Mufti Adab: The Anecdote of al-Tahawi and His Daughter
Anecdote illustrating al-Tahawi's sensitivity to ambiguous language and its lesson for mufti conduct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key lesson in mufti adab from the anecdote of al-Tahawi and his daughter, and apply the principle of avoiding ambiguous language in fatwa and teaching.

Core Idea
A mufti must be cautious in language to avoid unintended implications; al-Tahawi's anecdote teaches the gravity of words.

The anecdote about al-Tahawi is a powerful lesson in adab al-mufti. It shows how a scholar's choice of words can inadvertently cause misunderstanding and shame. This lesson unpacks the incident and draws principles for ensuring clarity and avoiding ambiguity in fatwa and teaching contexts.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote carefully
Read the narrative from the source text. Note the setting: al-Tahawi dictating questions to his daughter.
The anecdote is a self-contained story within the biography.
2
Identify the ambiguous word
The word 'jima'' (جامعنا) has two possible meanings: 'discussion/agreement' and 'sexual intercourse'. Understand how the context could lead to the second meaning.
In fiqh, jima' is often used for marital relations; in general Arabic, it also means 'collect' or 'discuss'.
3
Analyze the misunderstanding
The daughter's smile indicates she understood the term in its vulgar sense. Al-Tahawi's realization shows his immediate shame.
His reaction—burning with anger, cutting off dictation, raising his hands—demonstrates extreme distress.
4
Reflect on the consequences
Al-Tahawi prayed for death and died within days. This underscores the seriousness of causing such a misunderstanding, especially from a scholar.
This is not a literal cause of death, but shows his profound sense of accountability and modesty.
5
Derive adab principles
From this anecdote, derive guidelines for a mufti: avoid ambiguous words, be precise in language, and maintain a sense of shame and responsibility.
These principles are part of adab al-mufti (etiquette of the mufti).

What is the primary lesson for a mufti from al-Tahawi's anecdote?
